Prophethood
beginner
8 min
Prophetic Proofs from Predictive Miracles
Al-Nasafi enumerates prophetic predictions as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how predictive prophecies from the Quran and Hadith serve as proofs of prophethood, and see specific examples from the Prophet's lifetime.

Core Idea
Predictive miracles confirm prophethood because only Allah can unveil the future.

Al-Nasafi presents a powerful argument for the truthfulness of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) by listing several accurate predictions he made about future events. These predictions range from the humiliation of the Jews foretold in the Quran to specific predictions about individuals and historical events. Each one came true exactly as stated, demonstrating that the Prophet spoke from divine knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repeated phrase 'ومن ذلك' which introduces each new example.
2
Identify the Quranic prophecy
Find the first example from the Quran (the verse about the Jews) and note how Al-Nasafi explains its fulfillment in every age.
3
List the non-Quranic predictions
Go through each 'ومن ذلك' example and write down what was predicted and how it was fulfilled.
There are about eight examples; some are closely related.
4
Reflect on accuracy
Ask yourself: Could these predictions be mere coincidences? How does the fulfillment strengthen belief in prophethood?
The passage argues that only a true prophet can foretell the unseen with such precision.
5
Consider the overall argument
Synthesize: How do these examples together build a cumulative case for prophethood?
The more examples, the stronger the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علمًا منهم أنهم لو تمنوا لماتوا لولا ذلك لفعلوا إظهارا لخلفه. وكقوله تعالى في اليهود: {ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الذِّلَّةُ أَيْنَ مَا ثُقِفُوا إِلَّا بِحَبْلٍ مِّنَ اللَّهِ} ومصداق هذا في اليهود بين في كل عصر ومصر؛ إذ لم ترفع لهم راية منذ يومئذ، ولا ثبت لهم سلطان، وكانت أمارة الذل والصغار والمسكنة عليهم بادية، وعلامة السخط واللعنة ظاهرة وإن كانوا يرجعون إلى ثروة من المال وكثرة من العدة والعتاد. وأما ما هو راجع إلى الإخبار عن الكائنات في المستقبل غير الكتاب فمنه قوله عليه السلام: "زُوِيَتْ لِيَ الْأَرْضُ فَأُرِيتُ مَشَارِقَهَا وَمَغَارِبَهَا، وَسَيَبْلُغُ مُلْكُ أُمَّتِي مَا زُوِيَ لِي مِنْهَا" وكان كما أخبر إذ لم يرد بذلك جميع المشارق والمغارب، وإنما أراد ما ينطلق في عرف الناس عليه اسم المشرق والمغرب لانصراف مطلق الكلام إلى ما هو المستعمل في مخاطبة المتعارف في مفاوضاتهم. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعدي بن حاتم الطائي: "كيف بك إذا خرجت الظعينة من أقصى قصور اليمن إلى قصور الحيرة لا تخاف إلا الله؟" قال عدي: قلت يا رسول الله، فكيف بطيئ ومقامها؟ قال: "يكفيها الله طيئ" (وهذا إخبار عن الأمر الذي يكون بعدهم لأنهم كانوا خائفين في حياته، فكان كما أخبر في زمن عمر فكانت المرأة تخرج من قبيلة طيئ باليمن وتجاوز البادية، ولا يعترض لها أحد بمكروه). ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار: "تقتلك الفئة الباغية" فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه" يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "إنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين". ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر" فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر رضي الله عنهما. ومن ذلك قوله: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء" وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين سنة.
Knowing from them that if they wished for death they would die, otherwise they would have done it to show their defiance. And like His saying, the Exalted, regarding the Jews: 'Humiliation has been stamped upon them wherever they are found, except by a rope from Allah' and the verification of this among the Jews is clear in every age and region; for no banner has been raised for them since that day, nor has any authority been established for them, and the mark of humiliation, lowliness, and abasement upon them is evident, and the sign of wrath and curse is manifest, even if they possess wealth and abundant equipment and weaponry. As for what pertains to informtation about future beings other than the Book, from that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded for me, so I was shown its eastern and western parts, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me of it.' And it was as he informed, for he did not intend by that all the easts and wests, but rather he intended what, in the customary usage of people, is called the east and the west, because absolute speech is directed to what is customary in addressing the conventional in their conversations. And from that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i: 'How will it be with you when a woman traveling in a litter sets out from the furthest forts of Yemen to the forts of al-Hirah, fearing none but Allah?' 'Adi said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, how about the banditry of Tayyi' and their encampments? He said: 'Allah will suffice her against Tayyi'' (And this is information about a matter that would occur after them, because they were afraid during his lifetime, and it happened as he informed in the time of 'Umar, as women would set out from the tribe of Tayyi' in Yemen and cross the desert, and no one would accost them with harm). And from that is that he announced the death of al-Najashi and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and the reports followed that he died on that day. And from that is his saying to 'Ammar: 'The rebellious faction will kill you' and he was killed on the day of Siffin with 'Ali. And from that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' meaning the one who will strike you on your head and dye your beard with the blood of your head, and 'Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And from that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the apostates, and the deviators.' And from that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar' so he informed us by this that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr and after Abu Bakr is 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both. And from that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then Allah gives the kingdom to whom He wills' and the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was thirty years.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood through predictive miracles. Al-Nasafi presents two broad categories: prophecies from the Quran (the verse about the Jews) and prophecies from the Prophet (peace be upon him) about future events. He begins with the Quranic prophecy that humiliation will be upon the Jews wherever they are found, except through a covenant from Allah. Al-Nasafi notes that this is evidently fulfilled in every age: the Jews never raised a banner or established a lasting state, and the signs of humiliation and wrath are apparent despite their wealth and armaments. Then he turns to non-Quranic predictions. He lists several: (1) The earth was folded for him, and he saw its east and west; his community's dominion would reach those lands. This was fulfilled, but not literally every place—only what people customarily call 'east' and 'west'. (2) He told 'Adi ibn Hatim that a woman traveling alone from Yemen to al-Hirah would fear no one but Allah, and indeed during 'Umar's caliphate it happened, as the banditry of Tayyi' ceased. (3) He announced the death of the Negus on the day he died, and companions received confirmation. (4) He told 'Ammar that 'the rebellious faction would kill you', and 'Ammar was killed at Siffin fighting with 'Ali. (5) He told 'Ali that the most wretched person after the one who hamstrung the she-camel is the one who would strike his head and dye his beard, and 'Ali was struck on the head when he was killed. (6) He told 'Ali he would kill the oath-breakers, apostates, and deviators, which 'Ali did in his wars. (7) He said to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar after him, informing that they would be caliphs. (8) He said the caliphate after him would be thirty years, which matched the reigns of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Each example shows that the Prophet's foreknowledge came true exactly, proving his truthfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these predictions are mere coincidences or allegorical.
Correction: The passage insists they are literal fulfillments, proving prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which prophetic prediction concerned the duration of the caliphate after the Prophet's death?
A) It will last until the Day of Judgment
B) It will be thirty years
C) It will be a hundred years
D) It will be passed to the Umayyads

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate predictions about future events, including the duration of the caliphate, the death of the Negus, and specific events, constitute undeniable proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet foretold that a woman would travel safely from Yemen to Syria, and indeed it happened exactly. What fear or obstacle in your own life are you clinging to that Allah has already promised to remove? Why do you hesitate to trust His promise fully?
?
‘Adi ibn Hatim, a former Christian, doubted the Prophet’s claim until he saw the literal fulfillment of this prophecy. Is there any area of your faith where you are withholding full acceptance because you have not yet seen the outcome? What would it take for you to surrender that doubt today?
?
The Prophet told ‘Ali that the most wretched person would strike his head and dye his beard. That happened despite the seeming impossibility of killing a companion of such standing. Take a moment: if you knew that every word the Prophet spoke would come true, how would you change your relationship with his Sunnah right now?

Prophethood

Predictive Miracles: The Negus, Ammar, and Ali
Al-Nasafi enumerates four prophecies about individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's predictions about specific individuals demonstrate his prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecies prove divine knowledge.

Al-Nasafi begins his argument by citing concrete instances where the Prophet foretold events that later occurred exactly as reported. These examples serve as clear evidence that his knowledge came from Allah, not from human speculation.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of examples
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the repeated phrase 'wa min dhālika' introducing each prophecy.
Each example is a self-contained proof.
2
Identify the four prophecies
Find the four distinct predictions: Negus's death, Ammar's killing, Ali's head wound, and Ali's victory over three groups.
3
Reflect on their fulfillment
Consider that all these events happened exactly as foretold. This consistency is the evidential force.
The examples are chosen from well-known historical events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبَّر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار: "تقتلك الفئة الباغية" فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه" يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين." ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر" فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر رضي الله عنهما. ومن ذلك قوله: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء" وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين سنة. ومن ذلك حديث ليلة الإسراء وما أخبر من أخبار عير قريش، وكان كما أخبر. ومن ذلك أنه ضلت له عليه السلام ناقة فأقبل يسأل الناس عنها فقال المنافقون: هذا محمد يخبركم خبر السماء وهو لا يدري أين ناقته، فصعد المنبر وحمد الله وأثنى عليه، وحكى قولهم ثم قال: إني لا أعلم إلا ما أعلمني ربي وقد أخبرني أنها في وادي كذا متعلق زمامها بشجرة فبادر الناس فوجدوها كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله لخالد بن الوليد حين بعثه إلى أكيدر بدومة الجندل: "أما أنكم ستأتونه فتجدونه يصيد البقر" فوجدوه كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام للعباس حين أسره: "افد نفسك وابني أخيك" يعني عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارث فإنك ذو مال فقال: لا مال عندي. قال: فأين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد، فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا ولعبد الله كذا ولفلان كذا؟ فقال العباس: والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم بهذا أحد غيري، وإنك لرسول الله وأسلم هو وعقيل. ومن ذلك ما كان يخبر أهل النفاق بما كانوا يقولون فيما بينهم ويبيتون ما لا يرضى من القول حتى كانوا من شدة تعنتهم يحذرون أن ينزل عليه سورة تنبئهم بما في قلوبهم، وأمثال ذلك كثير، وكتابنا هذا يضيق عن ذكر عشر ذلك فضلاً عن كله، والله الموفق. ثم إن جميع ما أخبر من الأخبار الكائنة في المستقبل خرج على ما أخبر من غير تمكن كذب أو حلف في شيء من ذلك لا كمثل أخبار الكهنة والمنجمين.
And among that is that he (the Prophet) announced the death of the Negus and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and reports followed that he died on that day. And among that is his saying to Ammar: 'The rebellious group will kill you,' so he was killed on the day of Siffin with Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' — meaning the one who strikes your head and dyes your beard from the blood of your head — so Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the renegades, and the deviators.' And among that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar,' so he informed us by this that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr and after Abu Bakr, Umar, may God be pleased with them both. And among that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then God gives sovereignty to whom He wills,' and the caliphate of the rightly-guided caliphs was thirty years. And among that is the hadith of the night of Isra' and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as he informed. And among that is that his, peace be upon him, she-camel was lost, and he began asking people about her, so the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you news of the heaven but does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and extolled Him, and recounted their words, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that she is in such-and-such valley, her halter entangled in a tree.' So the people hastened and found her thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed, you will come to him and find him hunting cows,' and they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your brother's sons' — meaning 'Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith — 'for you are wealthy.' So he said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth you placed in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl, with no one else with you, and you said: If I am struck in my journey, then such-and-such is for al-Fadl, such-and-such for 'Abdullah, and such-and-such for so-and-so?' Then al-Abbas said: 'By Him who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knows this except me, and you are indeed the Messenger of God,' and he and 'Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is what he used to inform about the people of hypocrisy, what they said among themselves and secretly plotted of speech that is not pleasing, until from the intensity of their obstinacy they feared that a chapter would be revealed to him informing them of what was in their hearts. And such examples are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it, and God is the granter of success. Then, all that he informed of news occurring in the future came out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or mistake in any of that, not like the news of soothsayers and astrologers.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative proof of prophethood through predictive miracles (i'jāz al-ikhbār bi-al-ghayb). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, lists several verified predictions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that demonstrate his truthfulness. The argument proceeds by enumeration: each example is introduced with 'wa min dhālika' (among that is), building a chain of evidence. The examples include: (1) the death of the Negus of Abyssinia, announced while the Prophet was in Medina; (2) the prophecy that Ammar ibn Yasir would be killed by the rebellious party, fulfilled at the Battle of Siffin; (3) the prophecy that the most wretched person would strike Ali's head, fulfilled by Ibn Muljam; (4) the prophecy that Ali would kill the oath-breakers (nakithūn), renegades (māriqūn), and deviators (qāsitūn); (5) the instruction to follow Abu Bakr and Umar, indicating the order of succession; (6) the prophecy that the caliphate after him would last thirty years, which matched the reign of the four rightly-guided caliphs; (7) the details of the Isra' night and the Quraysh caravan, which came true; (8) the incident of the lost she-camel, where the Prophet accurately described its location; (9) the prophecy that Khalid ibn al-Walid would find Ukaydir hunting cows; (10) the revelation of the hidden wealth of al-Abbas, which led to his conversion; (11) the exposure of the hypocrites' secret conversations. After listing these, the author states that there are many more such examples, but his book cannot contain them all. Finally, he draws the conclusion: all these future reports came to pass exactly as predicted, without any falsehood or error—unlike the predictions of soothsayers (kahana) and astrologers (munajjimun), who often err. This distinction establishes that the Prophet's knowledge is from divine revelation, not from human guesswork.

Key Terms
النبوة
الإخبار بالمغيبات
إعجاز

Checkpoint
Which of the following did the Prophet foretell according to this passage?
A) The death of Abu Bakr
B) The killing of Ammar by the rebellious group
C) The victory of the Quraysh at Badr
D) The length of the caliphate

Key Takeaway
The fulfillment of specific prophecies about individuals confirms that the Prophet's knowledge comes from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
These prophecies were fulfilled precisely. Is your trust in the Prophet's knowledge merely intellectual, or does it translate into obedience in areas where his teachings seem difficult or counter to your desires?
?
The Prophet knew about events after his death, including the fates of individuals. If you truly believe that, how does it change the way you approach his commands regarding the unseen—like the punishment of the grave or the Day of Judgment?
?
Consider the prophecy about Ali being struck on the head. The Prophet named the most wretched person. Do you ever reflect on your own potential to be among the wretched if you persist in a sin or doubt that you know is wrong? What will you change today to avoid that?

Prophecies About Succession and the Caliphate
Al-Nasafi cites prophecies about succession and the Isra' event.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's predictions about leadership and future events prove his prophethood.

Core Idea
Predictions about political events also prove divine origin.

Al-Nasafi continues with prophecies about the caliphate and the night journey. These examples show that the Prophet's knowledge extended to political and historical events that later unfolded exactly as described.

Guided Path
1
Read the three prophecies
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how each prophecy is about future leadership or events.
The prophecies are: order to follow Abu Bakr and Umar, 30-year caliphate, and details of Isra'.
2
Analyze the fulfillment
Check that Abu Bakr and Umar indeed succeeded, the rightly-guided caliphate lasted 30 years, and the caravan news from Isra' matched.
These are historical facts.
3
Connect to the argument
Understand that these predictions could not have been guessed, so they indicate divine revelation.

ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبَّر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار: "تقتلك الفئة الباغية" فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه" يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين." ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر" فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر رضي الله عنهما. ومن ذلك قوله: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء" وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين سنة. ومن ذلك حديث ليلة الإسراء وما أخبر من أخبار عير قريش، وكان كما أخبر. ومن ذلك أنه ضلت له عليه السلام ناقة فأقبل يسأل الناس عنها فقال المنافقون: هذا محمد يخبركم خبر السماء وهو لا يدري أين ناقته، فصعد المنبر وحمد الله وأثنى عليه، وحكى قولهم ثم قال: إني لا أعلم إلا ما أعلمني ربي وقد أخبرني أنها في وادي كذا متعلق زمامها بشجرة فبادر الناس فوجدوها كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله لخالد بن الوليد حين بعثه إلى أكيدر بدومة الجندل: "أما أنكم ستأتونه فتجدونه يصيد البقر" فوجدوه كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام للعباس حين أسره: "افد نفسك وابني أخيك" يعني عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارث فإنك ذو مال فقال: لا مال عندي. قال: فأين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد، فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا ولعبد الله كذا ولفلان كذا؟ فقال العباس: والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم بهذا أحد غيري، وإنك لرسول الله وأسلم هو وعقيل. ومن ذلك ما كان يخبر أهل النفاق بما كانوا يقولون فيما بينهم ويبيتون ما لا يرضى من القول حتى كانوا من شدة تعنتهم يحذرون أن ينزل عليه سورة تنبئهم بما في قلوبهم، وأمثال ذلك كثير، وكتابنا هذا يضيق عن ذكر عشر ذلك فضلاً عن كله، والله الموفق. ثم إن جميع ما أخبر من الأخبار الكائنة في المستقبل خرج على ما أخبر من غير تمكن كذب أو حلف في شيء من ذلك لا كمثل أخبار الكهنة والمنجمين.
And among that is that he (the Prophet) announced the death of the Negus and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and reports followed that he died on that day. And among that is his saying to Ammar: 'The rebellious group will kill you,' so he was killed on the day of Siffin with Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' — meaning the one who strikes your head and dyes your beard from the blood of your head — so Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the renegades, and the deviators.' And among that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar,' so he informed us by this that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr and after Abu Bakr, Umar, may God be pleased with them both. And among that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then God gives sovereignty to whom He wills,' and the caliphate of the rightly-guided caliphs was thirty years. And among that is the hadith of the night of Isra' and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as he informed. And among that is that his, peace be upon him, she-camel was lost, and he began asking people about her, so the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you news of the heaven but does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and extolled Him, and recounted their words, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that she is in such-and-such valley, her halter entangled in a tree.' So the people hastened and found her thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed, you will come to him and find him hunting cows,' and they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your brother's sons' — meaning 'Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith — 'for you are wealthy.' So he said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth you placed in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl, with no one else with you, and you said: If I am struck in my journey, then such-and-such is for al-Fadl, such-and-such for 'Abdullah, and such-and-such for so-and-so?' Then al-Abbas said: 'By Him who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knows this except me, and you are indeed the Messenger of God,' and he and 'Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is what he used to inform about the people of hypocrisy, what they said among themselves and secretly plotted of speech that is not pleasing, until from the intensity of their obstinacy they feared that a chapter would be revealed to him informing them of what was in their hearts. And such examples are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it, and God is the granter of success. Then, all that he informed of news occurring in the future came out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or mistake in any of that, not like the news of soothsayers and astrologers.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative proof of prophethood through predictive miracles (i'jāz al-ikhbār bi-al-ghayb). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, lists several verified predictions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that demonstrate his truthfulness. The argument proceeds by enumeration: each example is introduced with 'wa min dhālika' (among that is), building a chain of evidence. The examples include: (1) the death of the Negus of Abyssinia, announced while the Prophet was in Medina; (2) the prophecy that Ammar ibn Yasir would be killed by the rebellious party, fulfilled at the Battle of Siffin; (3) the prophecy that the most wretched person would strike Ali's head, fulfilled by Ibn Muljam; (4) the prophecy that Ali would kill the oath-breakers (nakithūn), renegades (māriqūn), and deviators (qāsitūn); (5) the instruction to follow Abu Bakr and Umar, indicating the order of succession; (6) the prophecy that the caliphate after him would last thirty years, which matched the reign of the four rightly-guided caliphs; (7) the details of the Isra' night and the Quraysh caravan, which came true; (8) the incident of the lost she-camel, where the Prophet accurately described its location; (9) the prophecy that Khalid ibn al-Walid would find Ukaydir hunting cows; (10) the revelation of the hidden wealth of al-Abbas, which led to his conversion; (11) the exposure of the hypocrites' secret conversations. After listing these, the author states that there are many more such examples, but his book cannot contain them all. Finally, he draws the conclusion: all these future reports came to pass exactly as predicted, without any falsehood or error—unlike the predictions of soothsayers (kahana) and astrologers (munajjimun), who often err. This distinction establishes that the Prophet's knowledge is from divine revelation, not from human guesswork.

Key Terms
الخلافة
الخلفاء الراشدين
الإسراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about the caliphate after him?
A) It would last forever
B) It would be thirty years
C) It would be for his family only
D) It would end immediately after him

Key Takeaway
Predictions about future leadership and historical events that came true affirm the Prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet foretold the exact order of succession for Abu Bakr and Umar. Do you recognize that God’s plan is precise and absolute? How does that certainty change the way you submit to His decrees in your own life?
?
Consider the thirty-year caliphate prediction. If you truly believe this was from God, then why do you sometimes struggle to accept other prophetic teachings that also come from the same source? What specific command of the Prophet do you find hardest to follow, and what stops you from surrendering to it?
?
The Prophet gave a detailed report about a caravan during the night journey. If you had been there and witnessed this, would you have believed instantly? Then why, when you read other parts of the Qur'an and Sunnah, do you allow doubts to linger? What concrete step can you take today to increase your certainty in the unseen reports of the Prophet?

Prophethood
beginner

Knowledge of the Unseen: Hidden Matters Exposed
Al-Nasafi relates three incidents of revealing hidden information.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's knowledge of hidden and private matters proves his prophethood.

Core Idea
Knowing what is hidden to others is a sign of divine revelation.

Al-Nasafi now presents examples where the Prophet revealed information that was completely unknown to others, such as the location of a lost camel, the whereabouts of a person, and a secret financial arrangement. These demonstrate that his knowledge spanned hidden realities.

Guided Path
1
Read the three stories
Read the Arabic and translation: lost camel, Khalid and Ukaydir, and the incident with al-Abbas.
Each story involves information only Allah could have revealed.
2
Identify the hidden element
For each, note what was hidden: camel's location, Ukaydir's activity, al-Abbas's secret money.
3
Consider the reaction
Notice how the hypocrites challenged him, and how al-Abbas was convinced. The fulfillment silenced critics.
Al-Abbas's conversion is a direct result.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hypocrites saw a trivial gap in the Prophet's knowledge and used it to deny his entire message. Have you ever rejected a clear truth because of a minor doubt or inconvenience? Will you repent and seek humility before Allah?
?
Al-Abbas's hidden secret was exposed by the Prophet, leading to his conversion. If Allah revealed the hidden sins of your heart to people today, would you still feel secure? What will you do to make your hidden life align with your public faith?
?
The Prophet repeatedly said, 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me.' Do you accept that all true knowledge comes from Allah, and that the Prophet's words are entirely reliable? Or do you still let your own reasoning overrule his guidance? Commit today to submit to the Prophet's teachings, even when they challenge your assumptions.

Prophethood

The Final Proof: Distinguishing Prophethood from Soothsaying
Al-Nasafi gives a final example and concludes with the distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi concludes his argument by contrasting the Prophet's perfect predictions with the imperfect ones of soothsayers.

Core Idea
Flawless accuracy sets prophethood apart from guesswork.

Al-Nasafi finishes with a summary: all the Prophet's future reports came true without any error, unlike the predictions of soothsayers and astrologers who often fail. This final point solidifies the argument that his knowledge is from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding section
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the mention of hypocrites and the general statement.
The passage starts with 'wa min dhālika mā kāna yukhbiru ahl al-nifāq...' and ends with the distinction.
2
Identify the two parts
First, the example of exposing hypocrites; second, the general conclusion that all prophecies were flawless.
3
Contrast with soothsayers
Understand the key difference: soothsayers sometimes err, but the Prophet never did.
This is the crux of the argument.

And among that is that he (the Prophet) announced the death of the Negus and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and reports followed that he died on that day. And among that is his saying to Ammar: 'The rebellious group will kill you,' so he was killed on the day of Siffin with Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' — meaning the one who strikes your head and dyes your beard from the blood of your head — so Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the renegades, and the deviators.' And among that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar,' so he informed us by this that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr and after Abu Bakr, Umar, may God be pleased with them both. And among that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then God gives sovereignty to whom He wills,' and the caliphate of the rightly-guided caliphs was thirty years. And among that is the hadith of the night of Isra' and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as he informed. And among that is that his, peace be upon him, she-camel was lost, and he began asking people about her, so the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you news of the heaven but does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and extolled Him, and recounted their words, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that she is in such-and-such valley, her halter entangled in a tree.' So the people hastened and found her thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed, you will come to him and find him hunting cows,' and they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your brother's sons' — meaning 'Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith — 'for you are wealthy.' So he said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth you placed in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl, with no one else with you, and you said: If I am struck in my journey, then such-and-such is for al-Fadl, such-and-such for 'Abdullah, and such-and-such for so-and-so?' Then al-Abbas said: 'By Him who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knows this except me, and you are indeed the Messenger of God,' and he and 'Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is what he used to inform about the people of hypocrisy, what they said among themselves and secretly plotted of speech that is not pleasing, until from the intensity of their obstinacy they feared that a chapter would be revealed to him informing them of what was in their hearts. And such examples are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it, and God is the granter of success. Then, all that he informed of news occurring in the future came out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or mistake in any of that, not like the news of soothsayers and astrologers.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative proof of prophethood through predictive miracles (i'jāz al-ikhbār bi-al-ghayb). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, lists several verified predictions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that demonstrate his truthfulness. The argument proceeds by enumeration: each example is introduced with 'wa min dhālika' (among that is), building a chain of evidence. The examples include: (1) the death of the Negus of Abyssinia, announced while the Prophet was in Medina; (2) the prophecy that Ammar ibn Yasir would be killed by the rebellious party, fulfilled at the Battle of Siffin; (3) the prophecy that the most wretched person would strike Ali's head, fulfilled by Ibn Muljam; (4) the prophecy that Ali would kill the oath-breakers (nakithūn), renegades (māriqūn), and deviators (qāsitūn); (5) the instruction to follow Abu Bakr and Umar, indicating the order of succession; (6) the prophecy that the caliphate after him would last thirty years, which matched the reign of the four rightly-guided caliphs; (7) the details of the Isra' night and the Quraysh caravan, which came true; (8) the incident of the lost she-camel, where the Prophet accurately described its location; (9) the prophecy that Khalid ibn al-Walid would find Ukaydir hunting cows; (10) the revelation of the hidden wealth of al-Abbas, which led to his conversion; (11) the exposure of the hypocrites' secret conversations. After listing these, the author states that there are many more such examples, but his book cannot contain them all. Finally, he draws the conclusion: all these future reports came to pass exactly as predicted, without any falsehood or error—unlike the predictions of soothsayers (kahana) and astrologers (munajjimun), who often err. This distinction establishes that the Prophet's knowledge is from divine revelation, not from human guesswork.

Key Terms
النفاق
الكهنة
المنجمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's predictions were like those of soothsayers—sometimes right, sometimes wrong.
Correction: The passage asserts that all his predictions came true without any falsehood or mistake, unlike soothsayers.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how do the Prophet's predictions differ from those of soothsayers?
A) They are more often correct
B) They never contain falsehood or mistake
C) They are about religious matters only
D) They are always vague

Key Takeaway
The perfect accuracy of all prophetic predictions distinguishes them from fallible human guesses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet knew the secrets of the hypocrites, then surely he knows the secrets of your heart. What are you hiding from Allah that you hope no one will ever discover? Today, repent sincerely and resolve to abandon that hidden sin, knowing that it is already exposed before the One who sent the Prophet.
?
The soothsayers and astrologers you may dismiss, but do you ever rely on sources other than the Quran and Sunnah for guidance about your future—such as horoscopes, fortune-telling apps, or 'trusted' advice from those who claim to foresee outcomes? How can you justify putting your trust in fallible human guesses when the Prophet's every prediction came true without error? Make a firm intention to consult only Allah's word and the Prophet's example for your decisions.
?
The lesson shows that the Prophet's truthfulness is proven by flawless accuracy. Stop and examine your own heart: do you truly believe in every single thing the Prophet reported about the unseen—angels, Paradise, Hellfire, the Day of Judgment—or do you harbor doubts that you have never admitted? If you find any uncertainty, take it as a serious spiritual disease and seek knowledge and dua to strengthen your yaqeen (certainty).

Prophethood

The Elephant Incident and the Honor of Mecca
Nasafi argues for Mecca's sanctity and the Prophet's truthfulness using the Elephant incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Elephant incident serves as a preparatory miracle (irhās) for the Prophet Muhammad and how its historical certainty (tawātur) establishes the honor of Mecca, thereby confirming the truthfulness of the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Elephant incident is a historically certain sign that proves Mecca's sanctity and the Prophet's truth.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents a layered argument that combines historical evidence, theological reasoning, and poetic testimony to defend the prophethood of Muhammad. He first explains the Elephant incident as a divine preparatory sign (irhās), then demonstrates its undeniable historical transmission (tawātur), and finally infers that a city honored by such a sign must be the birthplace of a true prophet. This lesson will guide you through Nasafi's reasoning and the evidence he marshals.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of irhās
Read the opening part of the passage where Nasafi explains that the destruction of the Abyssinians was not for their faith but as an irhās for the coming of the Prophet. Notice how he connects this to God's protection of the Prophet's supporters.
Irhās are miraculous events that occur before a prophet's mission to prepare the way.
2
Recognise the strength of tawātur
In the middle section, Nasafi asserts that the Elephant incident is established by tawātur (mass transmission), making denial impossible. He quotes poets and the Quran to show widespread acknowledgment. Consider why tawātur is considered definitive proof in Islamic theology.
Tawātur means a report transmitted by so many chains that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.
3
Connect the honor of Mecca to the Prophet's truthfulness
Read the concluding argument: because Mecca was honored with such a clear sign (the Elephant incident), it is the most deserving place for a true prophet. Therefore, any denial of the Prophet from Mecca is obstinacy. Reflect on how this links historical evidence to theological conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قصدهم من الحبشان كانوا من أهل الكتاب مؤمنين بموسى وعيسى عليهما السلام متمسكين بكتابيهما التوراة والإنجيل، فلا يظن إهلاكهم لنصرة من كانت حالته تلك بل كان ذلك إرهاصا لأمر نبيه المصطفى محمد عليه السلام إذ كان قرب زمانه ودنا أوان خروجه وظهور دعوته، فصان الله تعالى الآباء لاحترام من علم الله تعالى خروجه من أصلابهم من أنصار دعوة رسول الله عليه السلام وأتباع ملته، ومتبعي دينه وشريعته، وحفظ نبيه الذي كان في سابق علمه قضائه أن يكون قبلة لأمته ومنسكا ومثابة لأهل ملته، ثم إن إنكار أمر الفيل ومبرم غير ممكن لأهل الإلحاد لثبوت ذلك بالتواتر الذي لا يتمكن فيه توهم الكذب كثبوت سائر الأمور الماضية في الأزمنة الخالية التي ينسب جاحدها إلى العناد والمكابرة، وقد ذكر ذلك الشعراء في قصائدهم والخطباء في مواعظهم. فمن ذلك قول نفيل بن حبيب وهو جاهلي، وكانت الحبشة أخذته في طريقها إلى مكة ليدلها فاحتال الهرب منها : ألا ردى ركائبنـ ا ردينـ فإنك لو رأيت ولن تراه حمدت الله إذ عاينت طيـ نعمناكم على الهجران عينا لدى جنب المخصب ما رأينا وحسب حجارة تلقــ علين وكلهم يسائل عن نفيل كأن عليَّ للحبشان دينـ وقال طفيل وهو جاهلي: ترعى مذانب وسمى أطماع لهـ بالجذع حيث عصى أصحابه الفيل وقال أبو الصلت أمية بن أبي الصلت ان آيات ربنـ ا بينـ نات جلس الفيل بالمغمس حتى ـــا يماري بهن إلا كفور ـل يحبو كأنه معقور وهذا في الجملة أشهر من أن يمكن إنكاره وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَكَيْفَ فَعَلَ رَبُّكَ بِأَصْحَب الْفِيلِ ﴾ إلى آخر السورة، ولم يعارضه أحد من المشركين بالتكذيب والرد لعلمهم بحقيقة ذلك بل قد كان بقى بعض من عاين ذلك الأمر ثم إن بلدة هذا شأنها أولى البلدان والبقاع بخروج من يدعو الخلق إلى الحق والدهماء إلى المحجة البيضاء، فكيف يستجير عاقل مقر بنبوة من خرج من مكانه لا مزية له على غيره من الأمكنة، ولا ظهر في الخلق له آية بينة تدل على حرمتها عند الله تعالى وكرامتها عليه أن ينسب الخارج عن البلدة المشهور شرفها المذكور فخرها الظاهر آياتها البين علاماتها إلى الكذب والافتعال والدعوة الظاهر عنها إلى التقول والمحال، وهذا واضح لمن ترك العناد وسلك سبيل الرشاد.
And among those who intended (Mecca) from the Abyssinians, they were People of the Book, believing in Moses and Jesus, peace be upon them, adhering to their books, the Torah and the Gospel. So one should not think that their destruction was for the sake of supporting one whose state was that. Rather, that was an  irhās (preparatory sign) for the matter of His chosen Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, since his time was near and the time of his emergence and the appearance of his call had drawn close. Therefore, God Almighty protected the fathers out of respect for those whom God knew would emerge from their loins as supporters of the call of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and followers of his community, and those who follow his religion and law. And He preserved His Prophet, who was in His prior knowledge and decree to be a qibla for his community, a place of sacrifice and a refuge for the people of his religion. Then indeed, the denial of the affair of the Elephant and its import is not possible for the people of atheism because it is established by tawātur (mass transmission) in which the possibility of falsehood cannot be conceived, like the establishment of all other past matters in bygone eras, whose denier is attributed to obstinacy and arrogance. Poets have mentioned it in their poems and orators in their sermons. Among that is the saying of Nufayl ibn Habib, who was a pre-Islamic poet, and the Abyssinians had taken him on their way to Mecca to guide them, so he contrived to escape from them: ... And the saying of Tufayl, who was pre-Islamic: ... And the saying of Abu 'l-Ṣalt Umayya ibn Abi 'l-Ṣalt: ... And this, in short, is more famous than can be denied. And God Almighty said: 'Have you not seen how your Lord dealt with the Companions of the Elephant?' to the end of the sūra. And none of the polytheists opposed it with denial or rejection because they knew the reality of that. Rather, some of those who witnessed that event remained. Then indeed, a town with this status is the most deserving of towns and regions for the emergence of one who calls creation to the truth and the masses to the pure path. So how can a reasonable person who affirms the prophethood of one who emerged from a place that has no merit over other places, and for whom no clear sign appeared among creation indicating its sanctity before God Almighty and His honor for it, attribute the one who emerged from the town whose honor is famous, whose glory is mentioned, whose signs are apparent, whose marks are clear, to lying and fabrication, and its manifest call to falsehood and impossibility? This is clear for one who abandons obstinacy and follows the path of guidance.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument: first, an explanation of the Elephant event as an irhās (preparatory miracle) for the Prophet Muhammad, then a proof of its historical certainty via tawātur, and finally a theological inference linking the honor of Mecca to the truthfulness of the Prophet. The author begins by noting that the Abyssinian attackers were Christians, but their destruction was not for supporting them; rather, it was a divine preparation for the coming of Muhammad. God protected the ancestors of the Prophet's supporters. The event is so well-known that denial is impossible—it is mutawātir, like other established historical facts. He then quotes three poets and the Quran to confirm widespread acknowledgment. The polytheists did not deny it because many had witnessed it. After establishing the event's certainty, Nasafi argues that Mecca, the site of this miracle, is uniquely honored; thus, any prophet emerging from it cannot be accused of lying. The rhetorical conclusion is that only the obstinate would reject this.

Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the Abyssinians were Christians, but their destruction was not for their faith; it was an irhās for the Prophet Muhammad, emphasizing that God's actions can have multiple purposes.

According to Nasafi, why is it impossible to deny the Elephant incident?

Key Takeaway
The Elephant incident is a mutawātir event that serves as an irhās, demonstrating the honor of Mecca and confirming the Prophet's truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Elephant incident is established by tawātur, yet many today treat it as a legend. Do you treat the historical proofs of your faith with the same certainty as everyday events? What would it take for you to be as certain of God's signs as you are of yesterday's news? Make a firm intention to verify at least one 'certain' story of faith this week.
?
God protected Mecca before the Prophet's call because He knew the Prophet would emerge from it. How does knowing that God's care precedes your awareness of His plan change the way you view the ordinary events of your life? Are you willing to see every safety and provision as a sign of a coming purpose? Commit to asking God daily: 'What are You preparing me for?'
?
The polytheists did not deny the Elephant incident because they knew its reality. When you encounter clear signs of God's power—in the Quran, in history, or in your life—do you submit, or do you explain them away? What is the 'obstinacy' Nasafi mentions that might be in your own heart? Resolve to surrender one area where you have been resisting the obvious truth for convenience.

Proof from the Place: The Honor of Mecca and the Elephant Incident
The author uses the Elephant incident to argue for Mecca's virtue as a proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the widely-known Elephant incident and the honor of Mecca serve as a proof for the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
Mecca's undeniable honor through the Elephant miracle proves it was fitting for a prophet to emerge from it.

This lesson explores an argument from 'place' used to support prophethood. The author cites the famous incident of the Elephant (the attack on Mecca by Abraha) as a universally acknowledged sign of Mecca's sanctity. By showing that Mecca's honor is beyond dispute, he argues that any rational person must accept the prophethood of one who emerged from such a blessed location. Let’s examine the passage step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the poetry and Quranic quotation used as evidence.
2
Identify the key elements
Find the poetry, the Quranic verse, and the historical fact about the Elephant incident. Observe how each is used to establish Mecca's honor.
3
Understand the logical connection
See how the author links Mecca's honor to the truthfulness of the Prophet: a town with such clear signs of divine favor is the fitting place for a true prophet.
Consider why the polytheists could not deny the incident.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that this proof is clear for anyone who abandons obstinacy. Ask yourself how this strengthens the case for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو الصلت أمية بن أبي الصلت:
ان آيات ربنـ ـا [؟] بينـ نات [؟] جلس الفيل بالمغمس حتى [؟] يمارى بهن إلا كفور [؟] يحبو كأنه معقور
وهذا في الجملة أشهر من أن يمكن إنكاره وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَكَيْفَ فَعَلَ رَبُّكَ بِأَصْحَاب الْفِيلِ﴾ إلى آخر السورة، ولم يعارضه أحد من المشركين بالتكذيب والرد لعلمهم بحقيقة ذلك بل قد كان بقى بعض من عاين ذلك الأمر ثم إن بلدة هذا شأنها أولى البلدان والبقاع بخروج من يدعو الخلق إلى الحق والدهماء إلى المحجة البيضاء، فكيف يستجير عاقل مقر بنبوة من خرج من مكانه لا مزية له على غيره من الأمكنة، ولا ظهر في الخلق له آية بينة تدل على حرمتها عند الله تعالى وكرامتها عليه أن ينسب الخارج عن البلدة المشهور شرفها المذكور فخرها الظاهر آياتها البين علاماتها إلى الكذب والافتعال والدعوة الظاهر عنها إلى التقول والمحال، وهذا واضح لمن ترك العناد وسلك سبيل الرشاد.
And Abu al-Salt Umayya ibn Abi al-Salt said: 'The signs of our Lord are clear... the elephant sat at al-Mughammas until... none disputes them except an ingrate... crawling as if crippled.' This is in general too well-known to be denied. And Allah Almighty said: 'Have you not seen how your Lord dealt with the companions of the elephant?' to the end of the surah. No polytheist opposed it with denial or rejection because of their knowledge of its reality. Rather, some who witnessed that event still remained. Then a town of this status is foremost among towns and regions for the emergence of one who calls creation to truth and the masses to the clear path. So how can a rational person who affirms the prophethood of one who emerged from a place that has no merit over other places, nor did any clear sign appear among creation indicating its sanctity before Allah and its honor to Him, attribute the one who emerged from the town whose honor is well-known, whose glory is mentioned, whose signs are manifest, whose marks are clear—to lying and fabrication, and his call to falsehood and impossibility? This is clear for whoever abandons obstinacy and follows the path of guidance.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the place (makān) of prophethood. The author begins by citing a line of poetry from Abu al-Salt that references the incident of the Elephant (the attack on Mecca by Abraha), then states that this event is too well-known to be denied. He reinforces this by quoting the Qur'anic surah al-Fil and noting that even the polytheists did not reject it because they knew it was true. Some eyewitnesses were still alive. The argument then proceeds: since Mecca is so clearly honored—through the Elephant miracle and its historic sanctity—it is the most fitting place for a prophet to emerge. Any rational person who accepts prophethood from such a place cannot then accuse that prophet of lying, because the place itself bears witness to divine favor. The conclusion is that this proof is evident for anyone who abandons stubbornness.

الفيل
شرف مكة
دليل النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Elephant incident is a legendary story with no historical basis.
Correction: The passage argues it was universally acknowledged and even polytheists accepted it; historical accounts and Quran confirm it.

Key Takeaway

The Pre-Islamic World as Evidence for Prophethood
Sanusi describes pre-Islamic corruption as proof of the need for a prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the widespread corruption and long interval between prophets serve as evidence for the necessity of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The desperate state of the world before Muhammad proves he was sent at the perfect time.

This passage from Tabṣirat al-Adilla presents a detailed proof from the time (zamān) of prophethood. Sanusi describes the moral and spiritual decay that had engulfed the Arabs, Persians, and Turks before Muhammad's mission. By painting this bleak picture, he argues that the world was in dire need of divine guidance, making the coming of a prophet not only plausible but inevitable. Read the passage carefully to see how he builds this case.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage fully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the rhetorical question and the detailed descriptions of three groups.
The passage is long but forms a single argument.
2
Identify the three groups
The author describes the Arabs, Persians, and Turks separately. Identify the specific corruptions attributed to each.
Arabs: idolatry, infanticide, plunder. Persians: fire-worship, hedonism, slavery. Turks: idolatry, destruction, oppression.
3
Analyze the rhetorical question
Sanusi asks if Allah would send messengers while previous laws were still strong and then abandon people. Understand the implied answer: no, which supports the need for a new prophet.
This connects Allah's habit of supporting religion to the timing of Muhammad's mission.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the cumulative evidence of corruption and the long interval makes the sending of a prophet not only plausible but necessary.
This is a key proof from the state of the world (dalīl al-zamān).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى زمانه فإنه بعث إلى الخلق في زمان كانت مدة الفترة بين الرسل فيه متطاولة، والشرائع بأسرها والحكم بأجمعها مندرسة، وآثار التخلف في الخلق بادية والهداة إلى الملة الحنيفية مغمورون معدومون، وأعلام الجور منصوبة، والطبيعة السبعية على الخلق متولية، كانوا يرون الأحق بالأمارة من كان أبعد في الإغارة، والأولى برياسة القبيلة والسيادة على العشيرة والفضيلة من كان أقدر على النهب وأحذق للطعن والضرب مع إجراء الله تعالى العادة بنصرته الدين عند ظهور أدنى دروس في معالمه، وتقوية أركانه عند ثبوت أيسر وهي أو وهن في دعائمه، أفترى الله تعالى يرسل رسلاً تترى بين موسى وعيسى عليهما السلام وشريعة التوراة باقية الآثار لائحة المنار كثيرة الأعوان قوية الأركان لحاجة وقعت إلى معرفة حكم جرى لا ذكر له في كتابهم ولا نص فيه عن نبيهم، ثم يرسل عيسى ليبدل مصلحة في أحكام قليلة العدد منقطعة المدد ، ثم يترك الناس والكفر قد طبق الأرض بأقطارها، والباطل ملأ الدنيا بأكنافها وأطرافها، وأكثر قبائل العرب اتخذوا الأصنام آلهة، ووأد البنات شريعة لازمة، والسعي في الأرض بالفساد عادة دائمة، والنهب والإغارة تجارة رابحة وسفك الدماء طبيعة الفرس اشتغلوا بعبادة النيران ووطء البنات والأمهات همتهم الأطعمة الشهية والأشربة المرية، استعبد أكابرهم الأصاغر ، واتخذ ملوكهم الرعايا خولا ، وأموالهم التي اكتسبوها بكد اليمين وعرق الجبين ،دولا، ويستعملونهم في حوائجهم استعمال النعم، ويصرفونهم يهمهم من الأمور تصريف العبيد والخدم لا يخلونهم وما تقتضي هممهم العليا راسخة، ونفوسهم الأبية من اقتناء أنواع العلوم وأصناف الحكم وأبواب الأدب. وجميع ممالك والترك يواظبون على تخريب ،البلاد، وتعذيب من ظفروا به من العباد وعادتهم الركض في طراف الأرض من الطول إلى العرض يسترق بعضهم البعض، يرون ارتكاب الجرائم واكتساب المآثم من أنفس الأعلاق والمغانم، دينهم عبادة الأصنام، ودأبهم ظلم الأنام.
As for what pertains to his time, he was sent to creation at a time when the period of the interval between messengers was prolonged, and all the laws and rulings were obliterated, and the traces of backwardness were apparent, and the guides to the hanifite religion were submerged and nonexistent, and the banners of tyranny were erected, and the beastly nature had taken charge over creation. They considered the one most deserving of leadership to be the one most skilled in raiding, and the one most entitled to chieftainship and sovereignty over the tribe to be the one most capable of plunder and most skilled in stabbing and striking—while Allah had the habit of supporting His religion when the slightest fading appears in its features, and strengthening its pillars when the slightest weakness appears in its supports. Do you think that Allah would send successive messengers between Moses and Jesus, peace be upon them, while the Torah's laws still had visible traces, clear beacons, many helpers, strong pillars, because of a need to know a ruling that occurred not mentioned in their book nor text from their prophet? Then He would send Jesus to change a benefit in a few rulings of limited duration, then He would leave the people while disbelief had covered the earth in its regions, and falsehood had filled the world in its sides and extremities; most Arab tribes had taken idols as gods, and burying daughters alive was a binding law, and spreading corruption in the land was a constant habit, and plunder and raiding were profitable trade, and bloodshed was natural. The Persians occupied themselves with fire-worship and violating daughters and mothers; their concern was delicious foods and bitter drinks; their great ones enslaved the small ones, and their kings took the subjects as property, and their wealth acquired by labor of hands and sweat of brows became states; they used them for their needs like cattle, and disposed of them as they wished like slaves and servants, not leaving them and what their high aspirations required—firm—and their noble souls from acquiring types of sciences and kinds of wisdoms and branches of literature. And all the kingdoms of the Turks persist in ruining lands, torturing those they capture from among the servants, and their custom is galloping across the face of the earth from length to width, enslaving each other; they consider committing crimes and acquiring sins as the choicest gains. Their religion is idol-worship, and their practice is oppressing people.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the time (zamān) of prophethood. The author details the state of the world before Muhammad's mission to show the necessity of a prophet. He lists: the long interval between prophets (fatrah), the obliteration of divine laws, the dominance of tyranny and beastly nature, and the moral corruption among Arabs (idol-worship, female infanticide, robbery, murder). He then contrasts this with Allah's usual practice of supporting religion when it weakens, implying that the need at that time was greatest. He describes the Persians as fire-worshippers obsessed with sensual pleasures, and the Turks as barbaric plunderers and idolaters. The overall picture is one of total spiritual and moral decay, making the sending of a prophet not only plausible but necessary. This serves as evidence that Muhammad's prophethood was timely and divinely ordained.

Key Terms
فترة
جاهلية
الطبيعة السبعية
الملة الحنيفية
أعلام الجور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The description of pre-Islamic Arabia as a time of ignorance (jāhiliyya) is exaggerated and not historically accurate.
Correction: Historical sources confirm that female infanticide, tribal warfare, and idolatry were widespread in pre-Islamic Arabia, as well as similar corruptions in Persia and Turkey. Sanusi's account aligns with these reports.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what was the state of the Arabs before Muhammad's mission?
A) They followed the Torah and awaited a prophet.
B) They were monotheists but lacked a scripture.
C) They practiced idolatry, female infanticide, and considered plunder a virtue.
D) They were ruled by just kings and had a high moral code.

Key Takeaway
The world's moral and spiritual decay before Muhammad demonstrates the necessity and timeliness of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had lived in that time of deep ignorance and darkness, what would your life have been like? How does that reality stir your gratitude for being born into the light of Islam? What are you actively doing to ensure you do not take this gift for granted?
?
The guides to the true religion were 'submerged and nonexistent.' In your own life, are there areas where your connection to the truth is becoming submerged by your desires, distractions, or the noise of the world? What concrete step will you take today to uproot that?
?
The Persians and Turks were consumed with indulgence (delicious foods and drinks) and oppression (enslaving others). What 'foods and drinks' or personal ambitions might be enslaving your heart and keeping you from standing for justice? How will you break free starting now?

Prophethood
beginner

The Necessity of Muhammad's Prophethood from Universal Corruption
Describes pre-Islamic ignorance and argues for the necessity of sending Muhammad as a messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the universal corruption before Islam proves the necessity of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The world's condition before Islam made a divine guide absolutely necessary.

This passage paints a vivid picture of pre-Islamic ignorance and corruption across various nations. By examining this universal decay, the author builds a compelling argument that only a divinely sent messenger could remedy it. The passage is a classic proof from the state of the world for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's descriptive tone and the rhetorical question at the heart of the argument.
Pay attention to the list of nations and their practices.
2
Identify the corrupted nations
List the groups mentioned: Arabs, Persians, Turks, Indians, Jews, Christians. Note the specific corruptions attributed to each.
This catalog of corruption is intentional.
3
Find the rhetorical question
Locate the question: 'Would He then leave the people thus bewildered...?' This is the pivot of the argument.
The question expects a negative answer.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that only Muhammad (s) could be the guide, supported by miracles and clear proofs.
He is described as the 'truthful, confirmed' one.
5
Reflect on the proof's strength
Consider why this argument is deemed sufficient even without other proofs. It appeals to divine wisdom and mercy.
The proof is rational, not merely emotional.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان أبعد في الإغارة، والأولى برياسة القبيلة والسيادة على العشيرة والفضيلة من كان أقدر على النهب وأحذق للطعن والضرب مع إجراء الله تعالى العادة بنصرته الدين عند ظهور أدنى دروس في معالمه، وتقوية أركانه عند ثبوت أيسر وهي أو وهن في دعائمه، أفترى الله تعالى يرسل رسلاً تترى بين موسى وعيسى عليهما السلام وشريعة التوراة باقية الآثار لائحة المنار كثيرة الأعوان قوية الأركان لحاجة وقعت إلى معرفة حكم جرى لا ذكر له في كتابهم ولا نص فيه عن نبيهم، ثم يرسل عيسى ليبدل مصلحة في أحكام قليلة العدد منقطعة المدد، ثم يترك الناس والكفر قد طبق الأرض بأقطارها، والباطل ملأ الدنيا بأكنافها وأطرافها، وأكثر قبائل العرب اتخذوا الأصنام آلهة، ووأد البنات شريعة لازمة، والسعي في الأرض بالفساد عادة دائمة، والنهب والإغارة تجارة رابحة وسفك الدماء طبيعة الفرس اشتغلوا بعبادة النيران ووطء البنات والأمهات همتهم الأطعمة الشهية والأشربة المرية، استعبد أكابرهم الأصاغر، واتخذ ملوكهم الرعايا خولا، وأموالهم التي اكتسبوها بكد اليمين وعرق الجبين، دولا، ويستعملونهم في حوائجهم استعمال النعم، ويصرفونهم يهمهم من الأمور تصريف العبيد والخدم لا يخلونهم وما تقتضي هممهم العليا راسخة، ونفوسهم الأبية من اقتناء أنواع العلوم وأصناف الحكم وأبواب الأدب. وجميع ممالك والترك يواظبون على تخريب البلاد، وتعذيب من ظفروا به من العباد وعادتهم الركض في طراف الأرض من الطول إلى العرض يسترق بعضهم البعض، يرون ارتكاب الجرائم واكتساب المآثم من أنفس الأعلاق والمغانم، دينهم عبادة الأصنام، ودأبهم ظلم الأنام. وجمهور الهند لا يعرفون إلا عبادة الأوثان وإحراق أنفسهم بالنيران. واليهود حرفوا الكلم عن مواضعها ودانوا بالتشبيه المحض إلا العنانية منهم فإنهم يقولون بثبوت الذات، وتعطيل الصفات، وجمعهم تكذيب المسيح عليه السلام. والنصارى متحيرون في دينهم مختلفون في مقالتهم فريق منهم يصف الله تعالى بالصاحبة والولد، وطائفة منهم يجعلون المسيح وأمه إلهين من دون الله إلى غير ذلك من المقالات الباطلة والجهالات الفاحشة، أفيترك الناس هكذا حيارى في دينهم يترددون، وفي طغيانهم يعمهون لا يرسل إليهم هاديًا ولا يبعث إلى الخلق داعيًا بل يتركهم وما يدينون من المحال ويعتقدون من الكفر والضلال وما يشتغلون به من السعي في الأرض بالفساد وتخريب البلاد وإهمال العقول والألباب عن اقتناء العلوم والآداب؟! هذا والله الظن الكاذب والوهم الباطل، ثم لا داعي في تلك الأيام، تأيد بالمعجزات والأعلام سواه، ولا هادي إلى ما يقتضيه العقل الصريح من التوحيد المحض والعبادات الخالصة وتوجيه السياسة الفاضلة من السنن العادلة ورفض الرسوم الجائرة والعادات الفاسدة، والأخلاق الدنية والخصال الذميمة غيره أعني به الصادق المصدق المؤيد بالأعلام الباهرة والمعجزات الظاهرة والدلائل الواضحة، والأمارات اللائحة صاحب الشريعة الزهراء والملة الغراء والمحجة اليبضاء، والدين القويم والصراط المستقيم محمد بن عبد الله بن عبد المطلب بن هاشم بن عبد مناف، صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهذه دلالة واضحة لو انعدم ما سواها من الدلائل لكانت كافية في التزام الحجة على من عدل عن المحجة، والله الموفق.
He was the farthest in raiding, and the most deserving of leadership of the tribe and chieftainship over the clan and excellence was the one most capable of plunder and most skilled in thrusting and striking, while Allah Almighty customarily supported His religion when the slightest trace of effacement appeared in its features, and strengthened its pillars when the least weakness or frailty occurred in its supports. Do you suppose that Allah Almighty sends successive messengers between Moses and Jesus, peace be upon them, while the law of the Torah remains with lasting traces, clear beacons, many helpers, and strong pillars, due to a need that arose for knowing a ruling that occurred with no mention of it in their book and no text about it from their prophet, then He sent Jesus to change some benefit in a few rulings of limited duration, then He leaves the people while disbelief has covered the earth in all its quarters, and falsehood has filled the world in its sides and extremities, while most Arab tribes took idols as gods, and burying daughters alive as a binding law, and spreading corruption in the earth as a permanent habit, and plunder and raiding as a profitable trade, and bloodshed as a nature. The Persians occupied themselves with fire-worship and intercourse with daughters and mothers; their concern was delicious foods and bitter drinks; their great ones enslaved the lesser ones; their kings took subjects as servants, and their wealth which they earned by the exertion of the right hand and sweat of the brow as revolving fortunes, and they used them for their needs as one uses cattle, and they directed them in matters as one directs slaves and servants; they did not leave them and what their lofty ambitions demanded, firmly rooted, and their noble souls, of acquiring types of sciences and kinds of wisdom and branches of literature. And all the kingdoms of the Turks persisted in destroying lands, and tormenting those they captured from among the people; their habit was to gallop across the earth from length to breadth, enslaving one another; they considered committing crimes and acquiring sins as the most precious spoils and gains; their religion is idol-worship, and their constant practice is oppressing people. And the multitude of India know nothing but worshipping idols and burning themselves with fire. And the Jews distorted words from their places and adhered to pure anthropomorphism, except for the 'Ananiyya among them, for they affirm the existence of the essence and denial of attributes, and collectively they deny the Messiah, peace be upon him. And the Christians are confused in their religion, differing in their doctrine: a group among them describes Allah Almighty as having a companion and a son, and a sect among them makes the Messiah and his mother two gods besides Allah, and other such false doctrines and ugly ignorances. Would He then leave the people thus bewildered in their religion, wavering, and in their transgression stumbling blindly, not sending them a guide, nor sending to creation a caller, but rather leaving them and what they follow of absurdity and believe of disbelief and error, and what they occupy themselves with of spreading corruption in the earth, destroying lands, and neglecting minds and intellects from acquiring sciences and literature? This, by Allah, is false assumption and vain fancy. Then there was no caller in those days supported by miracles and signs other than him, and no guide to what pure reason requires of pure monotheism, sincere acts of worship, and directing virtuous policy through just laws, and rejecting unjust customs, corrupt habits, base morals, and blameworthy traits other than him. I mean by that the truthful, the confirmed, supported by dazzling signs, manifest miracles, clear proofs, and evident marks, the possessor of the radiant law, the illustrious community, the white highway, the upright religion, the straight path: Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim ibn Abd Manaf, peace be upon him. And this is a clear proof; if all other proofs were absent, it would suffice to establish the argument against those who deviate from the path. And Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) based on the universal corruption and ignorance that prevailed before his mission. The author begins by describing the pre-Islamic condition, where the criteria for leadership were based on raiding and violence. He then poses a rhetorical question: after Allah sent messengers between Moses and Jesus to address specific needs, and after Jesus came with limited changes, would He then leave people in a state where disbelief and falsehood fill the earth, with Arabs worshipping idols, burying daughters alive, and engaging in plunder; Persians worshipping fire and practicing incest; Turks destroying lands and enslaving each other; Indians worshipping idols and self-immolation; Jews distorting scripture and falling into anthropomorphism or denial of attributes; Christians confused, some attributing a partner or son to Allah, others worshiping Jesus and Mary? The author argues that it is impossible for Allah to leave people without a guide, and that only a messenger supported by miracles could lead them to true monotheism, proper worship, and just governance. He identifies this guide as Muhammad (peace be upon him), the possessor of clear proofs. The passage concludes that this argument alone is sufficient to establish the proof against anyone who turns away from the truth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is merely emotional rhetoric, not a rational proof.
Correction: The argument is a rational proof of necessity based on the principle that divine wisdom cannot allow such corruption without guidance. It is a logical deduction from the state of the world.

Checkpoint
What is the main rhetorical device used in this passage to argue for the necessity of Muhammad's prophethood?
A) An analogy between previous prophets
B) A description of the corrupt state of the world before Islam, followed by a rhetorical question
C) A direct quote from previous scriptures
D) A logical syllogism about divine attributes

Key Takeaway
The universal corruption before Islam serves as a clear proof that Allah must have sent a guide, and that guide is Muhammad (s).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before Islam, people valued power, wealth, and status above truth. When you examine your own priorities, do you find any residue of that jahili mindset? What one thing are you willing to sacrifice today to align your values more with tawheed?
?
The passage describes a world in desperate need of guidance. Are you truly grateful for the guidance of Islam, or have you become complacent? If you were to lose access to the Qur'an and Sunnah for just one day, how would you feel?
?
This argument proves that Allah does not leave people without a guide. Do you feel that in your own life, you are actively seeking that guidance, or are you ignoring the signs that Allah has sent you? What step will you take today to respond to the call of the Prophet (s) in a way you haven't before?
