Religious Confusion and the Need for a Prophet
Al-Nasafi lists religious errors of Hindus, Jews, Christians, then argues for necessity of a prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi uses the state of religious confusion among Hindus, Jews, and Christians to argue for the necessity of prophethood and the exclusive guidance of Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
God's guidance through prophets is evident from the chaos of human religious error.

This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a sweeping survey of the religious state of three major communities known in the author's time: Hindus, Jews, and Christians. By cataloguing their errors—from idolatry to anthropomorphism to trinitarian excesses—al-Nasafi frames a powerful question: Would God leave humanity in such confusion without a guide? He then supplies the answer: Prophet Muhammad, supported by clear proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the rhetorical question towards the end.
2
Identify errors of each group
List the specific errors al-Nasafi attributes to Hindus, Jews, and Christians. Note the exception among Jews (the 'Ananiyya).
This sets up the need for guidance.
3
Understand the rhetorical question
Al-Nasafi asks whether God would leave people bewildered without a guide. Answer the question in your own mind.
The implied answer is 'No'.
4
Identify Muhammad as the guide
Find how al-Nasafi describes Prophet Muhammad and the proofs he brought. Note his lineage and titles.
He is the only caller with miracles in that era.
5
Recognize the proof argument
Al-Nasafi concludes that the existence of error and the presence of a prophet with signs constitutes a sufficient proof. Understand why this is a binding argument.
This is a proof from the state of the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجمهور الهند لا يعرفون إلا عبادة الأوثان وإحراق أنفسهم بالنيران. واليهود حرفوا الكلم عن مواضعها ودانوا بالتشبيه المحض إلا العنانية منهم فإنهم يقولون بثبوت الذات، وتعطيل الصفات، وجمعهم تكذيب المسيح عليه السلام. والنصارى متحيرون في دينهم مختلفون في مقالتهم فريق منهم يصف الله تعالى بالصاحبة والولد، وطائفة منهم يجعلون المسيح وأمه إلهين من دون الله إلى غير ذلك من المقالات الباطلة والجهالات الفاحشة، أفيترك الناس هكذا حيارى في دينهم يترددون، وفي طغيانهم يعمهون لا يرسل إليهم هاديًا ولا يبعث إلى الخلق داعيًا بل يتركهم وما يدينون من المحال ويعتقدون من الكفر والضلال وما يشتغلون به من السعي في الأرض بالفساد وتخريب البلاد وإهمال العقول والألباب عن اقتناء العلوم والآداب؟! هذا والله الظن الكاذب والوهم الباطل، ثم لا داعي في تلك الأيام، تأيد بالمعجزات والأعلام سواه، ولا هادي إلى ما يقتضيه العقل الصريح من التوحيد المحض والعبادات الخالصة وتوجيه السياسة الفاضلة من السنن العادلة ورفض الرسوم الجائرة والعادات الفاسدة، والأخلاق الدنية والخصال الذميمة غيره أعني به الصادق المصدق المؤيد بالأعلام الباهرة والمعجزات الظاهرة والدلائل الواضحة، والأمارات اللائحة صاحب الشريعة الزهراء والملة الغراء والمحجة اليبضاء، والدين القويم والصراط المستقيم محمد بن عبد الله بن عبد المطلب بن هاشم بن عبد مناف، صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهذه دلالة واضحة لو انعدم ما سواها من الدلائل لكانت كافية في التزام الحجة على من عدل عن المحجة، والله الموفق.
And the majority of the Hindus know only idol worship and burning themselves with fire. And the Jews distorted words from their places and adhered to pure anthropomorphism except for the 'Ananiyya among them, for they affirm the essence and negate the attributes, and all of them deny the Messiah, peace be upon him. And the Christians are perplexed in their religion, differing in their doctrine: a group among them describe God Almighty with a consort and child, and a sect among them make the Messiah and his mother two gods besides God, and other such false doctrines and obscene ignorances. Then are people left thus bewildered in their religion, wavering, and in their transgression wandering blindly, not sending to them a guide, nor sending to the creation a caller, but rather leaving them with what they profess of absurdity and believe of disbelief and misguidance, and what they occupy themselves with of corruption in the land and destruction of cities and neglect of intellects and minds from acquiring knowledge and manners?! This, by God, is a false assumption and an invalid fancy. Then there was no caller in those days, supported by miracles and signs, other than him, and no guide to what sound reason requires of pure monotheism and pure acts of worship and directing virtuous policy through just traditions and rejecting unjust customs and corrupt habits, base morals and blameworthy traits besides him—I mean the truthful, the believed, the supported by brilliant signs and manifest miracles and clear proofs and evident marks, the possessor of the radiant Sharia and the glorious religion and the white path, and the upright faith and the straight path: Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Abdul Muttalib ibn Hashim ibn Abd Manaf, may God bless him and grant him peace. And this is a clear proof; even if all other proofs were absent, it would suffice to establish the argument against whoever deviates from the path. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage provides a multi-layered argument for the necessity of prophethood. It first describes the religious state of the three major non-Muslim communities known to the author: Hindus, Jews, and Christians. Hindus are noted for idolatry and self-burning. Jews are described as distorting scripture and largely committing anthropomorphism, except for a group ('Ananiyya) who affirm God's essence but deny attributes; all deny Jesus. Christians are described as divided: some ascribe a spouse and child to God, others deify Jesus and Mary. After cataloguing these errors and their harmful social consequences (corruption, destruction, neglect of knowledge), the author poses a rhetorical question: Would God leave people in such confusion without sending a guide? He declares this is unthinkable. He then asserts that the only such guide in his time is Prophet Muhammad, detailing his title and lineage. Finally, he states that this scenario—the existence of error and the presence of a prophet with clear proofs—constitutes a sufficient proof for God's guidance, making the argument binding upon anyone who rejects it.

Key Terms
التشبيه المحض
التوحيد المحض
الحجة
الدعاة
المعجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God does not care about human guidance or leaves people to their own devices.
Correction: The passage argues that the existence of religious confusion and error demands divine guidance, which came through Prophet Muhammad with clear proofs.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the state of the Jews regarding divine attributes?
A) They all affirm anthropomorphism.
B) Most affirm anthropomorphism except the 'Ananiyya who negate attributes.
C) They all deny attributes.
D) They believe in a consort and child for God.

Key Takeaway
The religious confusion of humanity is itself a proof that God sends prophets, with Prophet Muhammad being the final and guiding proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Nasafi says it is a 'false assumption' to think God would leave people bewildered. In your own life, where have you assumed God's guidance is absent—in your confusion about a decision, a trial, or a doubt—and what would it mean to actively seek the prophetic guidance that God has already sent?
?
Look at the three groups: Hindus, Jews, Christians. Each held deep errors but also had fragments of truth. Which of your own beliefs or practices might be a mixture of truth and error? This lesson argues that the only complete guide is Muhammad. What is the one area where you have been mixing other influences into your faith, and what step will you take tonight to purify it?
?
The passage says the proof is sufficient 'even if all other proofs were absent.' If you were stripped of every external evidence—no scholars, no books, no community—would the internal evidence of the prophet's message and the state of humanity still compel you to believe? If not, what is lacking in your heart's certainty?

The Need for a Just Ruler and the Decline of Persia
Historical argument for prophethood through need for just rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the historical decline of the Persian kingdom serves as evidence for the human need for a just ruler, which in turn supports the necessity of prophethood.

Core Idea
The collapse of mighty kingdoms shows humanity’s desperate need for divinely guided leadership.

This lesson explores a unique argument for prophethood: not only do people need spiritual guidance, but they also need a just political authority. Using the fall of the Persian Empire and other ancient kingdoms as evidence, the author demonstrates that without a just ruler, society falls into chaos, and people cry out for a guide. This argument connects the political order to the mission of the Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for its flow, then read the translation. Notice how the author builds a case from human need to historical decline to divine mercy.
The passage ends mid-sentence; we will cover the full argument as given.
2
Identify the analogy
The author draws a parallel between the need for a teacher of religion and the need for a just ruler. Find where this comparison is made.
3
Analyze the Persian example
Examine the detailed description of Persia's might and its decline due to the king's claim to divinity. Note the consequences: weak rulers, women and boys in power, oppression.
4
Connect to prophethood
See how the people's fear and swearing leads to God sending Muhammad (peace be upon him). This shows that prophethood fulfills both spiritual and political needs.
The argument is that the human condition pre-Islam was unbearable, and only divine intervention could bring justice and security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يؤيد ما ذكرنا أن الناس كما كانوا محتاجين إلى من يعلمهم مصالح الدارين ويبين لهم معالم الدين، ويرشدهم إلى الحق، ويهديهم إلى سبيل الخير، ويوقفهم على نهج العبادة لخالقهم، وأداء شكر نعمه عليهم، كانوا متحاجين إلى من يسوسهم سياسة فاضلة، ويقبض على يدي القوى وينصر الظلوم وينصفه من ظالمه، ويمكن الدهماء ويؤمن الطرق، ويطفئ نائرة الفتن الواقعة في الأرض، لا يتقاضى الممالك المؤثلة، وانحلال قوى الولايات القديمة كان ملك فارس، وكان ملوكهم أعز ملوك الأرض وأشدهم شوكة، وأقواهم بطشاً، وأكثرهم عدة وعديدة ذخائر، وأعمرهم ولاية، قد ضعف، وتكاثر أسباب الخلل في قواعده وأركانه، وتداعى إلى الانعدام ما طال وعرض من بنيانه لشؤم ما كان بملكهم أبرويز من ادعاء الألوهية حتى نهى عن ذلك على لسان مغنية فأربد فقصمه الله تعالى وسلط ابنه شيرويه عليه فقتله، ثم كان يدوم لمن استولى منهم على الملك مدة ولا يشتد له شوكة، وآل الأمر إلى نصب النساء بأمور المملكة وتفويض الأمر إلى الصبيان، وكان لا يشتغل الواحد منهم للقيام بأسباب السياسات وضبط المملكة، وامتدت الأيدي الخاطئة والأطماع الفاسدة إلى الرعية بالإجحاف والاستئصال. وكذا ملك اليمن انتقض باستيلاء السودان عليه، وملك الحيرة بقتل أبرويز النعمان بن المنذر، وملك آل جفته وهم الغسانيون كان آل للضعف وأشرف على البطلان والزوال، وبقى الناس بعد انتقاض هذه الممالك أو ضعف أركانها وزوال السياسة وحفظ الحوزة والذب عن حريم الرعية خائفين وجلين طالبين من الله تعالى حسن الفرج مقسمين بالله جهد أيمانهم لئن جاءهم نذير ليكونن أهدى من إحدى الأمم. فرحم الله خلقه وبعث محمدًا نبيه، وبدلهم من بعد خوفهم أمنًا، وبعد اضطراب
What we have mentioned is supported by the fact that, just as people needed someone to teach them the interests of the two abodes [this world and the Hereafter] and explain to them the landmarks of religion, guide them to the truth, lead them to the way of good, and make them aware of the path of worship of their Creator and the performance of gratitude for His favors upon them, they were also in need of someone who would govern them with a virtuous policy, restrain the hands of the strong, help the oppressed and give him justice against his oppressor, enable the common people, secure the roads, and extinguish the flames of seditions occurring in the land—without demanding accumulated kingdoms and [preventing] the dissolution of powers of the ancient provinces. There was the kingdom of Persia: its kings were the most honored kings of the earth, the strongest in force, the most powerful in might, the most numerous in troops and treasures, and the most populous in dominion. [Yet] it weakened, and the causes of defect multiplied in its foundations and pillars, and its long and wide structure collapsed into non-existence because of the ill omen of what their king Abruwiz [Khusraw Parviz] did in claiming divinity, to the extent that he forbade [speaking] about that through the tongue of a singing girl, so he became enraged, and God Almighty crushed him and gave his son Shirwaih power over him, so he killed him. Then whoever among them seized the kingship would endure for a while but not become strong, and the matter came to appointing women to the affairs of the kingdom and entrusting affairs to boys, and none of them would occupy himself with undertaking the means of governance and control of the kingdom, and the wrongful hands and corrupt ambitions extended toward the subjects with oppression and extermination. Likewise, the kingdom of Yemen was dissolved by the domination of the Sudanese over it, and the kingdom of Hira by Abruwiz's killing of al-Nu'man ibn al-Mundhir, and the kingdom of the house of Jafna—they are the Ghassanids—ended up in weakness and approached annihilation and disappearance. So the people, after the dissolution of these kingdoms or the weakening of their pillars and the disappearance of governance and protection of the domain and defense of the sanctity of the subjects, remained fearful and anxious, asking God Almighty for a good relief, swearing by God with their strongest oaths that if a warner came to them, they would surely be more guided than any of the [other] nations. Then God had mercy on His creation and sent Muhammad, His Prophet, and changed their fear into security, and after disturbance...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents a supporting argument for the necessity of prophethood by focusing on the human need for political leadership and social order. It begins by drawing an analogy: just as people needed a prophet to teach them religion and guide them, they also needed a just ruler to maintain justice and security. The author then provides a historical case study: the Persian kingdom, once the mightiest, weakened and collapsed due to the sin of King Khusraw Parviz (Abruwiz) who claimed divinity. His punishment led to a chain of decline, with weak rulers, women and boys placed in power, and oppression of subjects. Similarly, the kingdoms of Yemen, Hira, and Ghassan declined. After the collapse of these powers, the people were left fearful and desperate, praying for relief, and they swore that if a warner came they would follow him—a reference to the Qur'anic verse (Fatir 42). God then responded by sending Prophet Muhammad, bringing security after fear. This argument ties the political chaos and human longing for justice to the divine mercy of sending a prophet who also establishes a just society.

Key Terms
السياسة الفاضلة
الممالك
الولايات
التنازع
الخوف
الأمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is only about historical cause and effect, not about prophethood.
Correction: The author uses history as evidence that humanity cannot achieve justice without divine guidance, thus proving the need for a prophet.

Checkpoint
What was the ultimate cause of the decline of the Persian kingdom according to the passage?
A) Military weakness.
B) The claim of divinity by their king Abruwiz.
C) Invasion by the Sudanese.
D) The rise of the Ghassanids.

Key Takeaway
The collapse of the Persian Empire and the people's desperate longing for a just guide demonstrates that prophethood is not only spiritual but also political, fulfilling humanity's need for a ruler who brings justice and security.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see political chaos and injustice in the world today, do you truly feel desperate for divine guidance, or have you become numb and complacent? The people of that time swore to follow a warner—would you if you lived then, or do you ignore the warnings that have already come?
?
Where in your own life have you acted like King Abruwiz, claiming a sense of self-sufficiency or divinity, deciding right and wrong without submitting to God? This passage shows that even the mightiest fall due to pride. What concrete step will you take this week to humble yourself before God in an area where you feel in control?
?
You already have the ultimate warner—the Qur'an and the Prophet (peace be upon him). But do you live as if you still need to be guided, or have you settled into your own way? This lesson teaches that true security comes only from God's guidance. Will you commit to reading the Qur'an with a heart that is genuinely open to change what needs to change in your life right now?

The Need for a Righteous Leader
Description of the ideal leader's functions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the qualities of ideal leadership that communities require, as described by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
True leadership brings guidance, justice, and security for all.

Before the advent of Islam, humanity was in dire need of a leader who could establish justice and guide them to truth. This passage from Imam al-Nasafi outlines the essential functions of such a leader, setting the stage for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). Let's explore what the author highlights as the core duties of a righteous ruler.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the list of responsibilities the author attributes to a virtuous leader.
The passage begins with 'ويبين لهم معالم الدين' describing the leader's role.
2
Identify the leader's duties
List the duties mentioned: explaining religion, guiding to truth, leading to goodness, teaching worship, gratitude, governing with virtuous policy, restraining the strong, helping the oppressed, securing roads, ending sedition.
This is a comprehensive vision of leadership.
3
Connect to pre-Islamic context
Understand that the author is setting up the background for why prophethood was needed. The absence of such leadership caused corruption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبين لهم معالم الدين، ويرشدهم إلى الحق، ويهديهم إلى سبيل الخير، ويوقفهم على نهج العبادة لخالقهم، وأداء شكر نعمه عليهم، كانوا متحاجين إلى من يسوسهم سياسة فاضلة، ويقبض على يدي القوى وينصر الظلوم وينصفه من ظالمه، ويمكن الدهماء ويؤمن الطرق، ويطفئ نائرة الفتن الواقعة في الأرض، لا يتقاضى الممالك المؤثلة، وانحلال قوى الولايات القديمة كان ملك فارس، وكان ملوكهم أعز ملوك الأرض وأشدهم شوكة، وأقواهم بطشاً، وأكثرهم عدة وعديدة ذخائر، وأعمرهم ولاية، قد ضعف، وتكاثر أسباب الخلل في قواعده وأركانه، وتداعى إلى الانعدام ما طال وعرض من بنيانه لشؤم ما كان بملكهم أبرويز من ادعاء الألوهية حتى نهى عن ذلك على لسان مغنية فأربد فقصمه الله تعالى وسلط ابنه شيرويه عليه فقتله، ثم كان يدوم لمن استولى منهم على الملك مدة ولا يشتد له شوكة، وآل الأمر إلى نصب النساء بأمور المملكة وتفويض الأمر إلى الصبيان، وكان لا يشتغل الواحد منهم للقيام بأسباب السياسات وضبط المملكة، وامتدت الأيدي الخاطئة والأطماع الفاسدة لا إلى الرعية بالإجحاف والاستئصال. وكذا ملك اليمن انتقض باستيلاء السودان عليه، وملك الحيرة بقتل أبرويز النعمان بن المنذر، وملك آل جفته وهم الغسانيون كان آل للضعف وأشرف على البطلان والزوال، وبقى الناس بعد انتقاض هذه الممالك أو ضعف أركانها وزوال السياسة وحفظ الحوزة والذب عن حريم الرعية خائفين وجلين طالبين من الله تعالى حسن الفرج مقسمين بالله جهد أيمانهم لئن جاءهم نذير ليكونن أهدى من إحدى الأمم. فرحم الله خلقه وبعث محمدًا نبيه، وبدلهم من بعد خوفهم أمنًا، وبعد اضطراب أمورهم واختلاف أحوالهم سكونا وقرارا، وبعد انتشار الظلم في الخليقة، وتطاير شرره في أصناف البرية عدلاً وإنصافا، فمن لم يقابل هذه النعمة بحسن القبول، ولم نفسه عاجزا عن أداء الشكر، فهو الكافر الجهول الذي لا دواء لدائه إلا الحسام القاضب لا حيلة لبرئه إلا الحمام الغالب، والله ولى العصمة وكاشف الغمة.
And to clarify for them the landmarks of religion, guide them to the truth, lead them to the path of goodness, stop them at the path of worship of their Creator, and performance of gratitude for His favors upon them, they were in need of someone to govern them with a virtuous policy, and to restrain the hand of the strong, and help the oppressed and give him justice from his oppressor, and enable the common people, and secure the roads, and extinguish the flame of seditions occurring in the land, not demanding the tributary kingdoms. And the dissolution of the forces of the old states: the kingdom of Persia was, and its kings were the most honored kings of the earth, the most formidable, the mightiest in power, most abundant in military equipment and treasures, and most prosperous in rule, had weakened, and the causes of corruption multiplied in its foundations and pillars, and what had long and wide of its structure collapsed to annihilation due to the ill omen of what was in their king Abrawiz of claiming divinity until he was rebuked for that by the tongue of a songstress, so he became angry, so Allah the Exalted destroyed him and subjected his son Shiruyah to him so he killed him. Then the rule would continue for whoever seized kingship among them for a time but his power did not strengthen. And the matter ended up with the appointment of women for the affairs of the kingdom and delegating the matter to boys, and not one of them occupied himself with undertaking the means of governance and controlling the kingdom. And the wrong hands and corrupt ambitions extended, not to the subjects with oppression and extermination. Likewise, the kingdom of Yemen was corrupted by the domination of the Sudan over it, and the kingdom of Hira by the killing of al-Nu'man ibn al-Mundhir by Abrawiz, and the kingdom of the house of Jafna, who were the Ghassanids, came to weakness and was close to extinction and disappearance. After the corruption of these kingdoms or the weakening of their pillars, the disappearance of governance, the preservation of territory, and defense of the subjects' sanctity, the people remained fearful and anxious, asking Allah the Exalted for a good relief, swearing by Allah with their most solemn oaths: 'If a warner comes to them, they will surely be better guided than one of the nations.' So Allah the Exalted had mercy on His creation and sent Muhammad His prophet, and changed for them after their fear security, and after the disorder of their affairs and the difference of their conditions tranquility and stability, and after the spread of injustice in creation and the scattering of its sparks among the kinds of creatures justice and equity. So whoever does not meet this blessing with good acceptance, and does not consider himself incapable of performing gratitude, then he is the ungrateful ignorant one for whose illness there is no remedy except the sharp sword, and no cure for his recovery except inevitable death. And Allah is the Master of protection and the Remover of distress.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological narrative. It begins by describing the need for a righteous leader who can establish justice, protect the weak, and maintain order. The author then surveys the decay of major pre-Islamic kingdoms: Persia, Yemen, Hira, and Ghassan. For Persia, he details the causes: the tyranny of King Abrawiz who claimed divinity, leading to internal strife and eventual collapse. The kingdom fell into weakness, with women and children ruling, and oppression of subjects. Similarly, Yemen fell to the Sudan, Hira was ruined by the killing of al-Nu'man, and Ghassan weakened. As a result, people lived in fear and prayed for relief, swearing that if a warner came, they would follow guidance. In response, Allah sent Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) as mercy, transforming fear into security and injustice into justice. The passage concludes by warning that rejection of this blessing leads to punishment, and only death can cure such ignorance.

Key Terms
معالم الدين
السياسة الفاضلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The primary role of a leader is only to maintain security and collect taxes.
Correction: The passage shows that a true leader also provides religious guidance, teaches worship, ensures justice, and refrains from exploitation.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a duty of a virtuous leader in the passage?
A) Teaching worship and gratitude
B) Building grand palaces
C) Securing roads
D) Restraining the strong

Key Takeaway
A righteous leader must combine spiritual guidance and worldly justice, securing both faith and safety for the people.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you seek guidance from a leader who combines spiritual teaching and worldly justice, or do you separate the two in your life, seeking one from scholars and the other from politicians? What does your answer reveal about your priorities?
?
When you witness oppression—whether in your community or globally—do you take any action to stop it, or do you remain passive? The ideal leader restrains the strong and helps the oppressed. What is your responsibility in this regard, starting today?
?
The passage describes a leader who does not demand tributary kingdoms—meaning he does not exploit others for his own benefit. In your daily interactions, do you ever take advantage of others for personal gain? How can you embody the selflessness of this ideal leader in your own conduct?

The Decay of the Persian Kingdom
Historical account of Persian decline due to king's tyranny.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the causes of the Persian empire's decline as presented by Imam al-Nasafi, focusing on the tyranny of King Abrawiz.

Core Idea
Tyranny and self-deification lead to divine punishment and collapse.

After establishing the ideal of virtuous leadership, the author turns to historical examples of corruption. The mighty Persian kingdom, once the most powerful on earth, fell due to internal decay. The key event was King Abrawiz's claim to divinity, which brought divine retribution. Let's examine the details of this downfall.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the description of Persia's former strength and subsequent weakness.
The passage begins with 'وانحلال قوى الولايات القديمة كان ملك فارس'.
2
Identify the cause of decay
Notice the author attributes the collapse to the ill omen of King Abrawiz's claim to divinity (ادعاء الألوهية).
This is a theological explanation for historical events.
3
Observe the consequences
List the outcomes: weakening of foundations, rise of internal strife, women and children rulers, oppression of subjects, and eventual destruction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبين لهم معالم الدين، ويرشدهم إلى الحق، ويهديهم إلى سبيل الخير، ويوقفهم على نهج العبادة لخالقهم، وأداء شكر نعمه عليهم، كانوا متحاجين إلى من يسوسهم سياسة فاضلة، ويقبض على يدي القوى وينصر الظلوم وينصفه من ظالمه، ويمكن الدهماء ويؤمن الطرق، ويطفئ نائرة الفتن الواقعة في الأرض، لا يتقاضى الممالك المؤثلة، وانحلال قوى الولايات القديمة كان ملك فارس، وكان ملوكهم أعز ملوك الأرض وأشدهم شوكة، وأقواهم بطشاً، وأكثرهم عدة وعديدة ذخائر، وأعمرهم ولاية، قد ضعف، وتكاثر أسباب الخلل في قواعده وأركانه، وتداعى إلى الانعدام ما طال وعرض من بنيانه لشؤم ما كان بملكهم أبرويز من ادعاء الألوهية حتى نهى عن ذلك على لسان مغنية فأربد فقصمه الله تعالى وسلط ابنه شيرويه عليه فقتله، ثم كان يدوم لمن استولى منهم على الملك مدة ولا يشتد له شوكة، وآل الأمر إلى نصب النساء بأمور المملكة وتفويض الأمر إلى الصبيان، وكان لا يشتغل الواحد منهم للقيام بأسباب السياسات وضبط المملكة، وامتدت الأيدي الخاطئة والأطماع الفاسدة لا إلى الرعية بالإجحاف والاستئصال. وكذا ملك اليمن انتقض باستيلاء السودان عليه، وملك الحيرة بقتل أبرويز النعمان بن المنذر، وملك آل جفته وهم الغسانيون كان آل للضعف وأشرف على البطلان والزوال، وبقى الناس بعد انتقاض هذه الممالك أو ضعف أركانها وزوال السياسة وحفظ الحوزة والذب عن حريم الرعية خائفين وجلين طالبين من الله تعالى حسن الفرج مقسمين بالله جهد أيمانهم لئن جاءهم نذير ليكونن أهدى من إحدى الأمم. فرحم الله خلقه وبعث محمدًا نبيه، وبدلهم من بعد خوفهم أمنًا، وبعد اضطراب أمورهم واختلاف أحوالهم سكونا وقرارا، وبعد انتشار الظلم في الخليقة، وتطاير شرره في أصناف البرية عدلاً وإنصافا، فمن لم يقابل هذه النعمة بحسن القبول، ولم نفسه عاجزا عن أداء الشكر، فهو الكافر الجهول الذي لا دواء لدائه إلا الحسام القاضب لا حيلة لبرئه إلا الحمام الغالب، والله ولى العصمة وكاشف الغمة.
And to clarify for them the landmarks of religion, guide them to the truth, lead them to the path of goodness, stop them at the path of worship of their Creator, and performance of gratitude for His favors upon them, they were in need of someone to govern them with a virtuous policy, and to restrain the hand of the strong, and help the oppressed and give him justice from his oppressor, and enable the common people, and secure the roads, and extinguish the flame of seditions occurring in the land, not demanding the tributary kingdoms. And the dissolution of the forces of the old states: the kingdom of Persia was, and its kings were the most honored kings of the earth, the most formidable, the mightiest in power, most abundant in military equipment and treasures, and most prosperous in rule, had weakened, and the causes of corruption multiplied in its foundations and pillars, and what had long and wide of its structure collapsed to annihilation due to the ill omen of what was in their king Abrawiz of claiming divinity until he was rebuked for that by the tongue of a songstress, so he became angry, so Allah the Exalted destroyed him and subjected his son Shiruyah to him so he killed him. Then the rule would continue for whoever seized kingship among them for a time but his power did not strengthen. And the matter ended up with the appointment of women for the affairs of the kingdom and delegating the matter to boys, and not one of them occupied himself with undertaking the means of governance and controlling the kingdom. And the wrong hands and corrupt ambitions extended, not to the subjects with oppression and extermination. Likewise, the kingdom of Yemen was corrupted by the domination of the Sudan over it, and the kingdom of Hira by the killing of al-Nu'man ibn al-Mundhir by Abrawiz, and the kingdom of the house of Jafna, who were the Ghassanids, came to weakness and was close to extinction and disappearance. After the corruption of these kingdoms or the weakening of their pillars, the disappearance of governance, the preservation of territory, and defense of the subjects' sanctity, the people remained fearful and anxious, asking Allah the Exalted for a good relief, swearing by Allah with their most solemn oaths: 'If a warner comes to them, they will surely be better guided than one of the nations.' So Allah the Exalted had mercy on His creation and sent Muhammad His prophet, and changed for them after their fear security, and after the disorder of their affairs and the difference of their conditions tranquility and stability, and after the spread of injustice in creation and the scattering of its sparks among the kinds of creatures justice and equity. So whoever does not meet this blessing with good acceptance, and does not consider himself incapable of performing gratitude, then he is the ungrateful ignorant one for whose illness there is no remedy except the sharp sword, and no cure for his recovery except inevitable death. And Allah is the Master of protection and the Remover of distress.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological narrative. It begins by describing the need for a righteous leader who can establish justice, protect the weak, and maintain order. The author then surveys the decay of major pre-Islamic kingdoms: Persia, Yemen, Hira, and Ghassan. For Persia, he details the causes: the tyranny of King Abrawiz who claimed divinity, leading to internal strife and eventual collapse. The kingdom fell into weakness, with women and children ruling, and oppression of subjects. Similarly, Yemen fell to the Sudan, Hira was ruined by the killing of al-Nu'man, and Ghassan weakened. As a result, people lived in fear and prayed for relief, swearing that if a warner came, they would follow guidance. In response, Allah sent Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) as mercy, transforming fear into security and injustice into justice. The passage concludes by warning that rejection of this blessing leads to punishment, and only death can cure such ignorance.

Key Terms
ملك فارس
أبرويز
الألوهية
شيرويه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Persian Empire fell primarily due to external invasions.
Correction: The author highlights internal moral decay, especially the king's claim to divinity, as the key cause.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the immediate divine punishment for King Abrawiz's claim to divinity?
A) His kingdom was invaded
B) His son killed him
C) He was struck by lightning
D) An earthquake destroyed his palace

Key Takeaway
Arrogance and claims to divinity invite divine punishment, leading to the collapse of even the mightiest kingdoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the arrogance of King Abrawiz claiming divinity, what is one area of your life where you act as if you are the ultimate authority, ignoring Allah's commands? What will you do today to surrender that area to Him?
?
The songstress spoke the truth to the king, and he became angry instead of repenting. Think of a recent time someone corrected you. Did you respond with humility or anger? What step can you take to seek forgiveness and practice humility?
?
The kingdom's collapse began when no one attended to governance. In your own responsibilities—whether in your home, work, or community—where have you neglected your duty due to pride? Commit to one specific action you will take this week to fulfill that duty with sincerity and humility.

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Collapse of Yemen, Hira, and Ghassan
Enumeration of fallen kingdoms and the people's desperation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how other pre-Islamic kingdoms (Yemen, Hira, Ghassan) also declined, leaving people in fear and longing for divine guidance.

Core Idea
When kingdoms fail, humanity cries out for a savior.

The Persian collapse was not an isolated event. The author briefly describes the downfall of other major kingdoms: Yemen fell to the Sudan, Hira was ruined by the murder of its king, and the Ghassanids weakened. With no strong leadership left, people lived in fear and prayed for a warner. This sets the stage for the coming of Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic covering the decay of Yemen, Hira, Ghassan, and the people's state.
The passage is short but rich in examples.
2
Identify each kingdom's fate
Note how each kingdom fell: Yemen to Sudan invasion, Hira through the murder of al-Nu'man, Ghassan to weakness.
3
Understand the people's response
The people became fearful and prayed, swearing to follow any warner who came.
This connects to the prophethood lesson.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face crises—personal or societal—do you truly turn to Allah in desperation, or do you rely on your own plans? The people in this lesson had no hope left but Allah. What is your first refuge?
?
The people swore by Allah that if a warner came, they would be better guided than any other nation. Are you living today as if you have already received that warner? Does your life reflect the guidance of the Prophet, or have you become complacent?
?
You are in a position to know the truth of prophethood. The people in this lesson only hoped for it. Are you using this knowledge to guide your actions and character, or are you taking it for granted? What specific change will you make today to be more guided than the nations who came before?

Prophethood
beginner

The Sending of Prophet Muhammad and the Divine Mercy
Description of the sending of the Prophet and its effects, with a warning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah responded to the desperate state of humanity by sending Prophet Muhammad as a mercy, bringing security and justice, and the warning for those who reject this blessing.

Core Idea
Divine mercy arrives in response to sincere desperation and transforms fear into peace.

After describing the decay of kingdoms and the fearful state of the people, Imam al-Nasafi presents the divine response: Allah sent Muhammad (peace be upon him) as a mercy. This resulted in the transformation of fear into security, disorder into tranquility, and injustice into justice. The passage ends with a stern warning for those who reject this blessing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic from 'فرحم الله خلقه' to the end. Notice the contrasts: fear to security, disorder to tranquility, injustice to justice.
2
Identify the transformation
List the pairs: fear → security, disorder → tranquility, injustice → justice and equity.
This shows the comprehensive change brought by the Prophet.
3
Understand the warning
The passage warns that rejecting this blessing leaves no cure except death. This emphasizes the seriousness of ingratitude.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sending of the Prophet was only for spiritual matters, not societal transformation.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the Prophet brought security, tranquility, and justice, showing a comprehensive societal impact.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Allah change for the people after sending the Prophet?
A) Their wealth increased
B) Fear into security, disorder into tranquility, injustice into justice
C) They gained political power
D) They became rulers

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad's advent was a comprehensive mercy that transformed society from fear to security, disorder to peace, and injustice to justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Allah sent Muhammad as a mercy to transform fear into security. Where in your life today are you still living in spiritual fear—whether of the future, of others' opinions, or of Allah's own judgment—that you have not yet surrendered to that prophetic mercy? What one step will you take this week to actively trust the security that comes from following the Prophet?
?
The passage warns that the one who does not accept this blessing with good acceptance and who does not feel incapable of showing gratitude is the 'ungrateful ignorant one'. Honestly, when you read about the Prophet's mission, do you receive it as a personal gift or do you feel entitled to it? When have you failed to feel the humility of being incapable of thanking Allah for sending the Prophet? How can you cultivate that humility today?
?
If Allah's mercy truly transformed disorder into tranquility, then why do so many Muslims—including yourself—live with inner turmoil and anxiety? What specific part of the Prophet's guidance are you neglecting that would bring that promised tranquility into your heart? Commit to implementing one sunnah this week that addresses a current anxiety.

Refutation of the Claim of Lost Counter-Texts to the Quran
Nasafi refutes the claim that counter-texts to the Quran existed but were lost.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that counter-texts to the Quran existed but were lost is rationally untenable based on the historical incentive to preserve them.

Core Idea
The enemies of Islam would have preserved any counter-texts, so their absence proves they never existed.

Nasafi addresses a potential objection to the miraculous nature of the Quran: that opponents produced similar texts but they were lost over time. This might seem plausible, but a closer look at the historical context reveals why it cannot be true. This lesson unpacks Nasafi's concise refutation, which hinges on the motives of the Quran's opponents.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the claim that counter-texts existed but were lost due to the dominance of Islam. This sets up the problem Nasafi refutes.
Notice that the objection tries to explain away the Quran's uniqueness.
2
Analyze Nasafi's response
Nasafi calls this claim 'extreme ignorance' and presents a logical counter-argument. Pay attention to the conditional reasoning: if counter-texts existed, the enemies would have transmitted them.
3
Reflect on the historical implication
Consider why the enemies' need to transmit counter-texts was pressing. What does this argument tell us about the Quran's status as a miracle?
This connects the lesson to broader discussions of prophethood and miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن زعم الجاحدون لرسالته الله أنهم عارضوه إلا أن ذلك صار مندرسًا لعلو كلمته وشيوع دعوته وشدة شوكة أتباعه وأشياعه. قيل لهم هذا جهل مفرط، فإنهم لو عارضوه وكان المنكرون له أكثر من متبعيه وأعداؤه أوفر عددًا وأقوى يدًا من أوليائه ؛ لكان ينبغي أن ينقل أولئك المعارض كما نقل هؤلاء القرآن إذ كانت حاجتهم إلى ذلك ماسة لدفع خصومهم من
If the deniers of His messengerhood claim that they opposed him, but that became extinct due to the high status of his word, the spread of his call, and the strength of his followers and partisans, it is said to them: This is extreme ignorance. For if they opposed him, and the deniers were more numerous than his followers and his enemies more numerous in number and stronger in power than his supporters, then it would be necessary that those counter-texts be transmitted just as the Qur'an was transmitted, because their need for that was pressing to repel their opponents from
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage refutes the argument that counter-texts to the Quran existed but were lost. Nasafi calls this claim extreme ignorance (jahl mufrit). He reasons that if such counter-texts existed, the enemies of Islam, who were more numerous and powerful at the time, would have preserved them to use against the Muslims. Their need for such material to refute the Quran was urgent, so it is inconceivable that they would not have transmitted it. The fact that no such texts have come down to us proves they never existed.

Key Terms
معارضة
مندرس
جهل مفرط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Historically significant texts can be accidentally lost even if they were important.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the enemies of Islam had a strong incentive to preserve any counter-Quranic texts, so their loss would be inexplicable. Therefore, the absence of such texts proves they never existed.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi reject the claim that counter-texts to the Quran existed but were lost?
A) Because the Muslims destroyed them.
B) Because the enemies of Islam would have preserved them to refute the Quran.
C) Because such texts are impossible.
D) Because the Quran itself says they didn't exist.

Key Takeaway
The claim that counter-texts to the Quran were lost is refuted by the fact that the enemies of Islam would have preserved them if they existed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The enemies of the Prophet would have preserved any counter-text because they needed it. Is there any truth you have rejected or ignored because acknowledging it would require you to change? What would it cost you to accept it?
?
If you were one of the deniers hearing Nasafi's argument, could you honestly find a flaw? Or would you be forced to admit the claim is false? What does your hesitation reveal about your own motives?
?
The absence of evidence is not always evidence of absence—but here it is. When in your life have you used the excuse 'maybe it got lost' to avoid facing the truth? Will you continue making excuses, or will you face the evidence?

Refuting the Lost Counter with Musaylimah's Example
Rebuts claim that opponents produced a counter lost due to Prophet's strength.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that opponents produced a counter-Quran that was lost is invalid, and how the example of Musaylimah proves this.

Core Idea
A lost counter is no counter at all; if it existed, it would have been transmitted.

This passage addresses a common objection: that the opponents did produce a counter to the Quran but it was suppressed by the Prophet's followers. The author refutes this as absurd, arguing that the opponents had every motive to preserve such a counter, and even Musaylimah's nonsense survived. This lesson unpacks that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening line where the opponents claim their counter was lost due to the Prophet's power. Note the three factors they cite: loftiness of his word, spread of his call, and power of his followers.
The objection is based on alleged suppression.
2
Author's initial response
See how the author dismisses the claim as 'extreme ignorance' (جهل مفرط). This sets the tone for the logical refutation.
Notice the directness of the rebuttal.
3
Logical argument
Follow the conditional reasoning: if the opponents were more numerous and powerful, they would have transmitted their counter to refute the Prophet. The absence of transmission proves its non-existence.
This is a key proof based on historical plausibility.
4
Example of Musaylimah
Observe the analogy: Musaylimah's incoherent speech survived despite Islam's strength. If a real counter existed, it would have survived similarly.
Musaylimah's example strengthens the argument from transmission.
5
Conclusion
Synthesize that the lack of any transmitted counter confirms the Quran's inimitability and the falsehood of the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن زعم الجاحدون لرسالته الله أنهم عارضوه إلا أن ذلك صار مندرسًا لعلو كلمته وشيوع دعوته وشدة شوكة أتباعه وأشياعه. قيل لهم هذا جهل مفرط، فإنهم لو عارضوه وكان المنكرون له أكثر من متبعيه وأعداؤه أوفر عددًا وأقوى يدًا من أوليائه؛ لكان ينبغي أن ينقل أولئك المعارض كما نقل هؤلاء القرآن إذ كانت حاجتهم إلى ذلك ماسة لدفع خصومهم من ألا ترى أن ما أتى به مسيلمة الكذاب من الهذيان كيف بقى وما هاجموا به رسول الله ( ) لم يرتفع ولم ينعدم لكثرة أعوان الإسلام وأنصاره، وقوة أشياع النبي وأتباعه.
For if the deniers of His messenger claim that they opposed him, but that became obliterated due to the loftiness of his word, the spread of his call, and the severity of the power of his followers and partisans—it is said to them: This is extreme ignorance. For if they had opposed him, and the deniers of him were more numerous than his followers and his enemies greater in number and stronger in hand than his supporters, then it would have been necessary that those countering be transmitted just as these transmitted the Quran, since their need for that was pressing to repel their opponents. Do you not see that what Musaylimah the liar brought of nonsense—how it remained? And what they attacked the Messenger of God with did not rise nor become extinct, despite the abundance of the supporters of Islam and its helpers, and the strength of the partisans and followers of the Prophet.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objectors claim that they did produce a counter to the Quran but it was lost because the Prophet's followers suppressed it. The author refutes this as extreme ignorance. He argues that if a counter had existed, it would have been transmitted by the opponents because they needed it to refute the Prophet, and the opponents were initially more numerous and powerful. Moreover, the author points to the example of Musaylimah the false prophet: his incoherent speech survived despite the strength of Islam. So if the opponents' alleged counter had existed, it would have survived as well. Its lack of transmission proves it never existed.

Key Terms
مندرِس
معارض
مسيلمة
هذيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that the lack of a recorded counter to the Quran could be due to suppression rather than the absence of any such counter.
Correction: The author argues that if a counter existed, the opponents, who were initially more numerous, would have preserved and transmitted it to refute the Prophet. The survival of Musaylimah's speech shows that even weak speech can be transmitted if it serves a purpose. Therefore, the absence of transmission proves no counter was ever produced.

Checkpoint
Why does the author use the example of Musaylimah the liar?
A) To show that false prophets are easily forgotten.
B) To demonstrate that even incoherent speech survives if it is widely transmitted.
C) To argue that the Quran's inimitability is due to its content.
D) To prove that the Prophet's followers suppressed all opposition.

Key Takeaway
The claim of a suppressed counter is baseless; the survival of Musaylimah's nonsense proves that any true counter would have been transmitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth because it was inconvenient, like the opponents claiming a lost counter? What truth are you avoiding today, and what will you do to confront it?
?
Musaylimah's nonsense survived—what does that mean for your own legacy? What will survive of your deeds, and are you building something that will stand the test of time?
?
The enemies had every reason to preserve a counter, yet none exists. How does this challenge your trust in the Quran's preservation? What does it demand from you in response?

The Challenge to Produce a Surah and the Refutation of Fear
Refutation of the fear excuse for not meeting the Quran's challenge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the excuse of fear as a reason for not producing a surah like the Quran.

Core Idea
If opponents already risk death by denying the Prophet, fear cannot excuse them from the challenge.

Having presented the Quran's challenge to produce a surah like it, the author now addresses a possible excuse: fear of reprisal from the Muslim community. He argues that this excuse is inconsistent because the opponents have already incurred the death penalty by their open denial. Moreover, historical figures like Ibn al-Rawandi openly attacked Islam without being stopped. This lesson examines this powerful rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author sets up the challenge, then anticipates the excuse of fear.
Pay attention to the rhetorical structure: challenge → excuse → refutation → examples.
2
Identify the inconsistency
The author points out that the opponents already speak against the Prophet and reject the argument, which itself warrants death. So why would they fear death from producing a counter?
3
Consider the secret option
If they claim to do it secretly, the author retorts that they can produce the counter secretly as well. This closes the loophole.
4
Examine the historical examples
Ibn al-Rawandi and Ibn Zakariyya wrote books attacking Islam without being prevented by fear. This proves that fear is not a real barrier.
These examples strengthen the argument by showing that others did it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول لهم : أنتم لن يعوزكم الكتبة (۳) البلغاء والخطباء والفصحاء، وفضلتم سادة العرب بضمكم إلى فصاحة العرب أنواع العلوم واشتغالكم بدرسها طول عمركم، وإحرازكم حكمة الهند وفلسفة اليونان وسياسة العجم، ثم أنتم المخاطبون بقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأْتُواْ بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِثْلِهِ (٤) مطالبون بذلك محجوجون به، فأتوا أنتم بمثله وعارضوه بشكله، فإن () زعمتم أنكم تخافون الحفاظ للملة الذابين عنها بالسيوف والرماح والعامة المتسارعين إلى (٦) إراقة الدماء من عرفوا منه القدح في الدين الذي يدينون به. قيل لكم ما لكم تجاسرتم على إظهار المخالفة وبسط اللسان في الرسول بالتكذيب، وفي الحجة بالجحود والرد واستحقاقكم القتل واستيجابكم إراقة الدماء به لا بإظهار )) ما يعارض الحجة ويقابل الدليل ؟ فإن قلتم : إنا نظهر المقالة سراً. قيل لكم: فأظهروا المعارض أيضا سرا. ثم نقول ما بال ابن الراوندي ) لم تمنعه هيبة الذابين عن الدين الناصرين له عن تصنيف كتاب التاج، وكتاب الزمرد وقضيب الذهب، وابن زكريا المتطبب (۹) لم يمنعه من ذلك عن تصنيف كتاب مخاريق الأنبياء وكتاب نقض الأديان، وجماعة
Then we say to them: You do not lack scribes, eloquent speakers, orators, and eloquent poets, and you have surpassed the lords of the Arabs by adding to the eloquence of the Arabs various sciences, occupying yourselves with their study throughout your lives, and acquiring the wisdom of India, the philosophy of the Greeks, and the politics of the Persians. Then you are the addressees of the Almighty's saying: 'Then bring a Surah like it' (2:23), demanded by that and argued against by it. So bring you its like and oppose it with its similar. If you claim that you fear the guardians of the religion who defend it with swords and spears, and the common people who hasten to shed blood of one known to have disparaged the religion they follow, it is said to you: What is the matter with you? You have dared to show opposition and to extend the tongue against the Messenger in denial, and against the argument in rejection and refutation, while deserving death and necessitating the shedding of your blood by that, but not by showing what opposes the argument and counters the proof? If you say: We show the statement secretly, it is said to you: Then show the counter secretly as well. Then we say: What is with Ibn al-Rawandi? The awe of the defenders of the religion and its supporters did not prevent him from composing the Book of the Crown, the Book of the Emerald, and the Rod of Gold; and Ibn Zakariyya the physician—the awe did not prevent him from composing the Book of the Fraud of the Prophets and the Book of the Refutation of Religions, and a group...
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a direct challenge to the opponents of the Quran. The author first notes that the opponents are well-equipped with eloquence, sciences, and wisdom, so they should be able to produce a surah like the Quran, as the Quran itself challenges them. If they claim fear of the Muslim community's swords as an excuse, he points out the inconsistency: they already openly slander the Prophet and reject the proof, which already incurs the death penalty, so why not produce a counter? If they say they do it secretly, then they can produce a counter secretly too. The author then cites historical examples: Ibn al-Rawandi and Ibn Zakariyya al-Razi (the physician) openly wrote books attacking religion without being prevented by fear, so the excuse of fear is invalid.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fear of persecution was a legitimate reason for the Arabs not to produce a text matching the Quran.
Correction: The author argues that the opponents already openly denied the Prophet, which itself carried the death penalty, so fear cannot be a genuine barrier. Moreover, historical heretics like Ibn al-Rawandi produced counter-works despite the risk.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the excuse that opponents were afraid to produce a counter to the Quran?
A) He claims they were not actually afraid.
B) He points out that they already dare to speak against the Prophet, so they should also dare to produce a counter.
C) He says the Quran's challenge applies only to believers.
D) He argues that the Quran is inimitable by its nature.

Key Takeaway
Fear of persecution is not a valid excuse for not meeting the Quran's challenge, as opponents already risk death by their denial.

?

?
The author shows that fear is inconsistent if you already risk death by denial. In what area of your life are you inconsistent—claiming to fear Allah but acting contrary to that fear? How will you align your actions with your claimed beliefs starting today?
?
The opponents risked death by denial but still denied. Are you willing to face the consequences of your choices for the sake of Allah? What is the greatest risk you are taking right now for your faith, and if none, what step will you take this week to put your faith above your comfort?

Refuting the Fear Excuse for the Qur'an's Inimitability
Nasafi refutes the fear excuse for not rivaling the Qur'an with historical counterexamples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the fear excuse for not producing a rival to the Qur'an is invalid, and how historical examples demonstrate that opponents had no fear but still failed.

Core Idea
Opponents failed to rival the Qur'an not from fear, but from sheer inability.

This passage tackles a common objection: that no one produced a rival to the Qur'an because they feared the Muslims' swords. Nasafi counters by pointing out that opponents openly attacked Islam in other ways without fear, yet never produced a rival. Their true reason was inability, not fear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Notice the confident tone as Nasafi dismantles the excuse.
Pay attention to the examples—they are the core of the refutation.
2
Identify the structure of the argument
The passage moves from a general observation (Musaylima's nonsense persisted) to a direct challenge, then refutes the fear excuse with historical examples, and concludes with inability as the real reason.
This is a typical kalām style: assertion, objection, refutation.
3
Reflect on the proof's strength
Ask yourself: Why does this argument seal the case for the Qur'an's inimitability? The examples show that even those who wrote whole books attacking Islam did not dare to produce a single comparable surah. That is the proof of 'ajz (inability).
This connects to the broader doctrine of i'jāz al-Qur'ān.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ألا ترى أن ما أتى به مسيلمة الكذاب من الهذيان كيف بقى وما هاجموا به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يرتفع ولم ينعدم لكثرة أعوان الإسلام وأنصاره وقوة أشياع النبي وأتباعه. ثم نقول لهم: أنتم لن يعوزكم الكتبة البلغاء والخطباء والفصحاء، وفضلتم سادة العرب بضمكم إلى فصاحة العرب أنواع العلوم واشتغالكم بدرسها طول عمركم، وإحرازكم حكمة الهند وفلسفة اليونان وسياسة العجم، ثم أنتم المخاطبون بقوله تعالى: {فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِّثْلِهِ} مطالبون بذلك محجوجون به، فأتوا أنتم بمثله وعارضوه بشكله، فإن زعمتم أنكم تخافون الحفاظ للملة الذابين عنها بالسيوف والرماح والعامة المتسارعين إلى إراقة الدماء من عرفوا منه القدح في الدين الذي يدينون به. قيل لكم ما لكم تجاسرتم على إظهار المخالفة وبسط اللسان في الرسول بالتكذيب، وفي الحجة بالجحود والرد واستحقاقكم القتل واستيجابكم إراقة الدماء به لا بإظهار ما يعارض الحجة ويقابل الدليل؟ فإن قلتم: إنا نظهر المقالة سراً. قيل لكم: فأظهروا المعارض أيضاً سراً. ثم نقول ما بال ابن الراوندي لم تمنعه هيبة الذابين عن الدين الناصرين له عن تصنيف كتاب التاج، وكتاب الزمرد وقضيب الذهب، وابن زكريا المتطبب لم يمنعه من ذلك عن تصنيف كتاب مخاريق الأنبياء وكتاب نقض الأديان، وجماعة التنويه بالبصرة لم يمنعه من تصانيف لهم كثيرة في نصرة قولهم بأصلين قديمين للعالم والطعن في الإسلام بل عن المجاهرة في المناظرة والمقابلة لدى المجادلة والاسفراري لم يمنعه ذلك عما صنف من أنواع الإلحاد وجماعة الباطنية لم يمنعهم ذلك عما صنفوا من الكتب لنصرة نحلتهم الرديئة وثلبهم الدين الظاهر كأبي حاتم الرازي والكوسج البزدوي والجاورساني وأبي علي وغيرهم ممن يطول ذكرهم حتى اشتهر كل ذلك، وانتشر في أداني بلدان الإسلام وأقاصيها، وبلغ جميع أطراف الأرض ونواحيها، والخلعاء والمجان لم يمنعهم ذلك من هجو الإسلام وشهر رمضان والصيام والصلاة وأشباه ذلك ومنعهم عن المعارضة وهي أشفى لصدورهم، وأشد تحصيلاً لفرضهم ومقصودهم، بل امتنعوا عن ذلك لعجزهم وقصورهم، فلزمتهم الحجة وانقطعت معذرتهم في الإعراض عنه؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، عجزوا عن ذلك لأنه كان أفصحهم لسانًا وأجودهم بيانًا على ما روى عنه عليه السلام أنه قال: "أنا أفصح العرب"، وذلك لا يدل.
Do you not see that what Musaylima the liar brought of nonsense persisted, and what they attacked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with did not rise nor disappear due to the many supporters of Islam and its helpers and the strength of the followers of the Prophet and his companions? Then we say to them: You do not lack scribes, eloquent speakers, orators, and eloquent poets; and you have surpassed the masters of the Arabs by adding to the eloquence of the Arabs the types of sciences, your occupation with their study throughout your lives, and your acquisition of the wisdom of India, the philosophy of the Greeks, and the politics of the Persians. Then you are the ones addressed by His statement: 'Then bring a surah like it'—you are required by it and refuted by it. So bring its like and oppose it with its match. If you claim that you fear the protectors of the religion who defend it with swords and spears and the common people who hasten to shed blood, of those who know from him (the critic) a slander against the religion they profess, it is said to you: What is the matter with you that you dare to show opposition and extend your tongue against the Messenger by denial, and against the proof by rejection and refusal, deserving killing and meriting the shedding of blood by that, and not by showing what opposes the proof and confronts the evidence? If you say: We show the statement secretly, it is said to you: Then show the opposition also secretly. Then we say: What is the matter with Ibn al-Rawandi that the awe of the defenders of the religion, the helpers of it, did not prevent him from composing the Book of the Crown, the Book of the Emerald, and the Golden Rod? And Ibn Zakariyya the physician was not prevented by that from composing the Book of the Tricks of the Prophets and the Book of the Refutation of Religions. And the group of al-Tanwih in Basra was not prevented from having many compositions in support of their statement of two ancient origins for the world and the attack on Islam, rather from open disputation and confrontation in debate. And al-Isfarari was not prevented by that from what he composed of types of heresy. And the group of al-Batiniyya were not prevented by that from what they composed of books to support their vile sect and their reviling of the apparent religion, like Abu Hatim al-Razi, and al-Kusaj al-Bazdawi, and al-Jawarsani, and Abu Ali, and others whose mention would be lengthy, until all that became famous and spread in the near and far cities of Islam and reached all parts of the earth and its regions. And the lowlifes and the mad were not prevented by that from satirizing Islam, the month of Ramadan, fasting, prayer, and the like of that; but they were prevented from opposition, which is more fulfilling for their hearts and more effective in achieving their purpose and intention. Rather, they refrained from it due to their inability and insufficiency; so the proof became binding on them and their excuse in turning away from it was cut off. If they say: Yes, they were unable to do that because he (the Prophet) was the most eloquent of them in tongue and the most excellent in expression, according to what was narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he said: 'I am the most eloquent of the Arabs,' and that does not indicate (the inability).
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the excuse that opponents of the Prophet were prevented from producing a rival to the Qur'an because they feared the Muslim defenders and the common people. Nasafi begins by noting the persistence of Musaylima's nonsense compared to the Prophet's challenge, indicating that if the opponents had a true rival, it would have remained. He then addresses the opponents directly: they have eloquent scribes, orators, and scholars; they surpass the Arabs in eloquence and learning; yet they are challenged by the Qur'anic verse 'then bring a surah like it.' They are obligated and refuted by this challenge. If they claim fear of death or harm, Nasafi points out that they openly engage in other forms of attack on the Prophet and Islam, which also incur the death penalty, so why do they not produce a rival if they are able? If they say they do these things secretly, then they can also produce a rival secretly. The author then provides historical examples: heretics like Ibn al-Rawandi and Ibn Zakariyya wrote books attacking Islam (e.g., 'The Tricks of the Prophets', 'The Refutation of Religions') without fear, yet they did not produce a rival to the Qur'an. Similarly, groups like al-Tanwih in Basra, al-Isfarari, and numerous Batini theologians authored explicit works of heresy and revilement of Islam, spreading far and wide. Even lowlifes and madmen openly mocked Islam, Ramadan, fasting, and prayer. Despite this lack of fear, they were prevented from producing a rival—not by fear, but by their sheer inability. Thus the argument (hujja) is established against them and their excuse is cut off. Finally, Nasafi anticipates the objection that the Prophet's superior eloquence made it impossible, but he notes this assertion itself does not prove inability, leaving the argument open. The passage is a classic proof of the inimitability (i'jāz) of the Qur'an, showing that fear does not explain the lack of rival attempts; only incapacity does.

Key Terms
حجة
عجز
معارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Opponents could not rival the Qur'an because they feared Muslim reprisal.
Correction: Historical evidence shows opponents openly wrote books attacking Islam and the Prophet without fear, yet never produced a rival, proving their failure was due to inability, not fear.

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of the examples of Ibn al-Rawandi and other heretics in this passage?
A) To show that these heretics were righteous scholars.
B) To argue that if they had been able to produce a rival to the Qur'an, they would have done so despite their fearlessness in writing against Islam.
C) To demonstrate that the Muslims were too weak to stop them.
D) To prove that the Qur'an is not a miracle.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's inimitability is proven by the fact that opponents, who freely attacked Islam in other ways, never produced a rival—showing their inability, not their fear.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are confronted with a clear command or challenge from Allah (like the Qur'an's challenge), do you find yourself making excuses to avoid responding? What is the real reason behind your hesitation?
?
The opponents openly attacked Islam in other ways, but never produced a rival surah. Reflect on your own life: what 'rivals' do you entertain that compete with the Qur'an in your heart? Are you truly unable to prioritize it, or do you hide behind excuses?
?
If you were to honestly assess your engagement with the Qur'an, would your actions show that you believe it is from Allah or that you treat it as just another book? What would change if you truly admitted your inability to match its words and submitted fully?

The Miraculous Eloquence of the Qur'an and the Impossibility of Human Origin
Nasafi argues that the Qur'an's sublime style and the Prophet's unlettered state prove its divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qur'an's profound theological content and unmatched eloquence constitute a miracle (i'jaz), especially given the Prophet's unlettered background.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's style and depth prove it cannot be from a man, let alone an unlettered one.

Imam Nasafi presents a compelling argument for the miraculous nature of the Qur'an. He first highlights the Qur'an's unparalleled eloquence and depth, then shows that even the most learned theologians have not exhausted its meanings. Finally, he argues that it is impossible for an unlettered man from an ignorant environment to have produced such profound arguments. This proves the Qur'an is from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the two main parts: the description of the Qur'an's style and the argument about the Prophet's background.
Notice the powerful language Nasafi uses to describe the Qur'an's effect on the intellect.
2
Understand the two-part argument
Identify how Nasafi first contrasts the Qur'an's speech with human speech, then presents the impossibility of an unlettered man producing such content.
The second part is a reductio ad absurdum: if the Prophet had produced it, he would have needed knowledge he could not have acquired.
3
Reflect on the implication
Recognize that this argument establishes the Qur'an as a miracle (i'jaz) and confirms the truth of the Prophet's message.
This argument is a standard proof of prophethood in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أن الله تعالى لا يخرج كلامه مخرج كلام الواحد منا إذا ناظر خصمه بل يخرج مخرج مخاطبة السادة العبيد، والأرباب المماليك، فأخرج هذه المعاني على هذا النظم العجيب والوصف البليغ الذي تكاد العقول الوافرة، والألباب الكاملة تتحير في رونقه وفخامته وبلاغته وفصاحته، بل تذهل من هيبته وجلالته، ثم إن المتكلمين من سلف الأمة منذ تكلموا في هذه الخصوم وأثبتوا دلائلها فى التصاريف لم يزيدوا على ما في الكتاب من مع الإشارة إلى ذلك، بل لم يستخرجوا من قعور تلك البحور وإن غاصت فيها أفكارهم هو المسائل عشر ما فيها من درر الحجج وغرر المعاني والنكت ثم من الممتنع الذي لا تصور لثبوته ولا يطلق العقل إخطاره بالقلب أن يخرج رجل أمي بلغ أشده، ومضى أربعين سنة من عمره في قوم لم يكن لهم من العلم بدلالة الكلام وحدوث العالم وثبوت الصانع وتوحيده وثبوت صفاته والبعث بعد الموت حظ، ولم يخطر ببال أحد منهم من ذلك، شيء، لم يقرعوا للتوحيد بابا، ويجعلون الأنداد والأصنام شيئًا عجابًا، لم يختلف إلى أحد للتعلم ولا درس كتابًا فيه شيء من ذلك ثم عرف من تلقاء نفسه جميع هذه الوجوه التي مر ذكرها بدلائلها، ثم بين على وجه قصر
But Allah the Exalted does not bring out His speech in the manner of speech of one of us when he debates his opponent. Rather, He brings it out in the manner of addressing masters to slaves and lords to servants. So He brought out these meanings in this wondrous composition and eloquent description at which abundant intellects and perfect minds almost become bewildered in its elegance, grandeur, eloquence, and clarity; indeed they become dazzled by its awe and majesty. Then indeed the theologians from the predecessors of the community, ever since they spoke about these disputations and established their proofs in the treatises, did not add anything beyond what is in the Book beyond indicating to that. Rather, they did not extract from the depths of those seas, even if their thoughts dived into them, one tenth of what is in them of pearls of proofs, best of meanings, and subtleties. Then it is impossible—which has no mental representation of its existence and the intellect does not allow its occuring in the heart—that an unlettered man, who reached his maturity and passed forty years of his life among people who had no share of knowledge of the indications of speech (kalam), origination of the world, establishment of the Maker, His unity, establishment of His attributes, and resurrection after death—and not a single thought of any of that occurred to any of them; they did not knock on any door for tawhid; they considered rivals and idols a wondrous thing; he did not attend any teacher nor study a book containing any of that—then he came to know from himself all these aspects that have been mentioned with their proofs, then he explained in a concise manner...
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the Qur'an is of human origin. The author first describes the sublime style of the Qur'anic discourse, comparing it to the speech of a master to a slave. Then he notes that even the most learned theologians have not exhausted its depths. Finally, he presents a reductio ad absurdum: it is impossible that an unlettered man who grew up in a completely ignorant environment could have produced such profound theological arguments. This proves the Qur'an is a miracle and the Prophet is truthful.

Key Terms
إعجاز
بلاغة
نظم
رجل أمي
دلائل الكلام
حدوث العالم
توحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet (saw) must have learned from scholars or traveled to gain knowledge to produce the Qur'an.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that the Prophet grew up in a society completely ignorant of theological arguments, never attended a teacher, and was unlettered, making it impossible for him to produce the Qur'an on his own.

Checkpoint
What makes it impossible that the Prophet (saw) produced the Qur'anic arguments himself?

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's unparalleled eloquence and profound teachings, combined with the Prophet's unlettered and uneducated environment, prove that the Qur'an is a divine miracle and not of human origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet, unlettered and in an ignorant environment, produced a book that even the greatest scholars cannot match. When you encounter doubt, do you let this reality settle in your heart, or do you brush it aside? What would it take for you to be utterly convinced that the Qur'an is divine?
?
If the Qur'an contains depths that scholars have barely scratched, how much of its wisdom have you personally extracted? Are you content with superficial reading, or will you commit to diving into its proofs and letting them transform your life?
